BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED AT BLUFFVIEW IN SAUK COUNTY
States News Service
July 12, 2010 Monday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 261 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: MADISON, WI
Body


The following information was released by the Wisconsin Department of Natural Resources:
A boil water advisory has been issued for residents of Bluffview, located along U.S. 12 in Sauk County about seven miles south of Baraboo, the state Department of Natural Resources reported Thursday afternoon.
All residents on the west side of Highway 12 are advised to boil their water prior to drinking or preparing food. Ice, food and any beverages prepared with unsafe water must be discarded. Persons in Bluffview should boil or use commercially bottled water for drinking, food preparation and making ice. If you boil water, the water should be heated to a rolling boil for at least one minute before use. Ice should be made from boiled or bottled water.
A water sample collected July 1 indicated the presence of coliform bacteria. Further sampling July 6 confirmed their presence. While coliform bacteria, naturally present in the environment, are not generally harmful themselves, they are an indicator that other, potentially-harmful, bacteria may be present.
Coliforms were found in more samples than allowed and this was a warning of potential problems. Whenever the DNR detects coliform bacteria in any sample, the department does follow-up testing to see if other bacteria of greater concern, such as fecal coliform or E. coli, are present. The department did not find any of these bacteria in subsequent testing.
The advisory will be lifted when there are two rounds of safe samples, said Dave Barkhahn, DNR water supply engineer. A notice will be issued when that occurs.

Load-Date: July 13, 2010

Penn Lifts Boil-Water Advisory
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
July 14, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 5
Length: 475 words
Byline: Civia Katz, Correspondent
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


BY CIVIA KATZ
Correspondent
Penn Township removed the boil-water advisory Tuesday, nearly three weeks after the public water supply tested positive for the parasite cryptosporidium.
Notices were hand-delivered to residents.
Cryptosporidium, a bacterium, was detected in the water on June 25. The state Department of Environmental Protection approved a plan for the township to flush out the system.
Dave Kratzer, township manager, said Monday the last two tests conducted by the township for the parasite came back negative.
The township had to wait 18-hours after running the normal bacteria test for E. coli and chloroforms on Monday before the DEP gave the all clear.
The township installed a portable filtering system at a cost of $25,000 per month to filter all township water. The system provides a 0.1 micron filtering system. The size of the cryptosporidium is 3 to 5 microns. Cryptosporidium bacteria are resistant to chlorine but can be filtered out or killed with high temperatures.
"There has not been untreated water entering the system since July 2," Kratzer said Monday.
The portable filtering system will remain in place until the permanent water filtration system is built and online, which is expected to next year. The project is expected to cost about $3 million.
After the bacteria alert, the township shut down its well and tapped into Manheim Borough's water supply to try to provide filtered water for the residents. Manheim Borough could not provide the amount of water needed because of poor infrastructure, Dave Sarley, Penn supervisor chairman, said Monday.
The borough has an aging system of pipes, and maps of the system are incomplete. Sarley said the borough has the water capacity, but not the facilities to support it.
The borough "had paved over a valve that was closed. They did not even know they had it. (Township Supervisor Daryl) Lefever found it and dug it up," said Sarley. "Five minutes after we hooked into borough water, people were out of water. There may be a lot of water there, but it could not get here."
The township had to put the well back online to supplement the water from the borough, Sarley said, and the township disconnected from the borough water system Monday.
He said the township has no plans to permanently connect to the borough water supply in the future.
The township provided residents with guidelines from the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention when the boil-water advisory was lifted. The guidelines advise residents to flush pipes and faucets.
Guidelines include running cold-water faucets continuously for five minutes, making and discarding three batches of ice from automatic ice makers, running water softeners through a regeneration cycle, draining and refilling water heaters set below 113 degrees Fahrenheit and changing filters on all point-of-entry and point-of-use water filters.

Load-Date: July 15, 2010


End of Document






NMED Lifts 'Boil Water Advisory' for Kamp Kiwanis in McKinley County
Targeted News Service
July 14, 2010 Wednesday 2:24 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 327 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's (NMED) Drinking Water Bureau advised the Kamp Kiwanis to lift a "boil water advisory" for its water system.
NMED issued the advisory after bacteriological contamination that exceeded the Maximum Contaminant Level for E. coli was discovered in drinking water from the water system. NMED required the Kamp Kiwanis non-community water system in McKinley County to notify its consumers of the finding.
Actions to disinfect the water system and identify possible sources of contamination were promptly taken. These actions included shock chlorination. Consumers were advised to boil all water prior to ingestion.
Water samples collected on July 10 and July 12, 2010 have shown no E. coli present in the water system. These clean results have allowed NMED's Drinking Water Bureau to advise Kamp Kiwanis to lift the "boil water advisory" for its water system.
The presence of E. coli in water indicates that the water may have been in contact with sewage or animal wastes, and could contain disease-causing organisms. Most strains of E. coli are harmless and live in the intestines of healthy humans and animals. However, a positive test for E. coli in the drinking water supply may indicate the presence of dangerous strains of E. coli or other disease-causing organisms, which are sometimes found in sewage or animal wastes. These types of organisms may cause severe gastrointestinal illness and, in rare cases, even death. Children, the elderly and immuno-compromised individuals are at an increased risk for illness.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or the DWB Water System Specialist Diane Barnes at 505-566-9744.
Contact: Marissa Stone Bardino, Communications Director, 505/827-0314, 505/231-0475
Copyright Targeted News Services
TNS hc11-JF78-100726-2928226 StaffFurigay

COLUMBIA, Mo., July 13 -- The city of Columbia issued the following news release:
A 6-inch water main on North Waterfront Drive broke early this morning which caused the pressure to drop substantially. According to standards set by the Department of Natural Resources, Columbia Water & Light issued a precautionary water boil advisory.
Customers living on North Waterfront Drive and Driftwood Court are urged to take the following precautions:
* Boil water for three minutes prior to using it for cooking or drinking.
* Do not use ice from an automatic ice maker. Remake ice with water that has been boiled.
* Disinfect dishes and food contact surfaces by immersing for one minute in clean tap water that contains one teaspoon of unscented bleach per gallon of water.
Crews are working on restoring water service to the area. Columbia Water & Light must have two clean samples before lifting the water boil advisory which will take a minimum of 48 hours for processing. Customers will be notified with phone calls and hang tags on their doors that the boil advisory has been lifted. Note, South Waterfront Drive customers are not included in the water boil advisory. For more information please contact: Sarabjit Jagirdar, Email:- htsyndication@hindustantimes.com

Residents Blast Workers, Officials Over Water Crisis; Nsupervisors Cited Threats Heard By Employees Who Were Trying To Fix Problem.
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
July 14, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 5
Length: 398 words
Byline: Civia Katz, Correspondent
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


BY CIVIA KATZ
Correspondent
About 20 residents vented their frustration over water contamination issues at the Penn Township meeting Monday, and the chairman of supervisors promised a better effort in the future.
The residents were upset after nearly three weeks of interrupted service because officials declared a boil-water advisory after cryptosporidium, a parasite, was found in public water.
Supervisors responded with concern about threats heard by township employees who were trying to fix the problem.
Dave Sarley, supervisor chairman, said the township was inundated with calls. Drivers yelled at workers trying to connect the township to the Manheim Borough waterlines, he said.
"A woman rolled her (car) window down and said, 'I hope you all die in that ditch.' I find this to be absolutely reprehensible," Sarley said. "These guys busted their butts so you'd have drinking water. You couldn't have gotten a more perfect storm with what we went through."
Sarley said the township placed workers under police protection while shifts ran 24-hours a day.
"We are not the community you have painted us. We are a caring community. All we wanted was to know," said Pat Drennen, board member of Brookshire Homeowners Association. "We tried to be on top of it to know what to do."
Some residents blamed the situation on the local farms.
Sarley said that cryptosporidium is everywhere. It is in human and animal feces, in the grass, in raccoons, in dogs and in mice.
The source of Penn Township water is the same aquifer that supplies water to Lititz and Manheim borough, Sarley said.
He also suggested that residents with private wells might want to have them tested.
The test for cryptosporidium is expensive and only done by specialized labs, Sarley said.
"Cryptosporidium has been around forever," he said. "Where we failed, we didn't get information to you on a daily basis. I think that is a valid criticism."
The township in responding to the crisis by collecting the phone numbers of all residents to make it faster and easier to get information out. In addition, the township will make daily updates when faced with a public crisis.
The township is in the process of obtaining permits to build a water filtration plant that will address cryptosporidium and nitrates. The plant will cost around $3 million.
"I promise in the future, if we get a major crisis, we will try to do better," Sarley said.

BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR THE CITY OF MINNEAPOLIS
States News Service
July 15, 2010 Thursday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 314 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: TOPEKA, KS
Body


The following information was released by the Kansas Department of Health and Environment:
The Kansas Department of Health and Environment (KDHE) has issued a boil water advisory for the City of Minneapolis, which is located in Ottawa County.
KDHE officials are issuing the advisory due to a break in a water main, which resulted in a loss of pressure in the distribution system. The water main is in the process of being repaired and whenever such a loss of pressure occurs, it is possible for contaminants to enter the system. Also during this time, disinfection (chlorine) residuals may drop to levels that are inadequate to protect against bacterial contamination.
Residents in the City of Minneapolis served by the affected public water system should observe the following precautions:
Boil water vigorously for one minute prior to use. Boiling longer than three minutes may adversely affect the quality and taste of the water.
Use only boiled water for drinking, brushing teeth, diluting fruit juices, and all other food preparation.
Dispose of ice cubes and do not use ice from a household automatic icemaker. Remake ice cubes with water that has been boiled.
Disinfect dishes and other food contact surfaces by immersion for at least one minute in clean tap water that contains one teaspoon of unscented household bleach per gallon of water.
Water used for bathing does not generally need to be boiled. Supervision of children is necessary while bathing or using backyard pools so water is not ingested. Persons with cuts or severe rashes may wish to consult their physicians.
The advisory will remain in effect until testing of water samples indicates no evidence of contamination and all other conditions which place the systems at risk of contamination are deemed by KDHE officials to be resolved. The city and/or KDHE will notify media when the boil water advisory has been rescinded.

Load-Date: July 16, 2010

Water Boil Advisory Lifted for North Waterfront Drive

July 15, 2010 Thursday 2:28 AM EST

State lifts boil water advisory in Bluffview
The Capital Times (Madison, Wisconsin)
July 16, 2010 Friday
ALL EDITION


Copyright 2010 Madison Newspapers, Inc. All Rights Reserved
Section: NEWS; Pg. WEB
Length: 240 words
Byline: By BILL NOVAK The Capital Times , bnovak@madison.com
Body


.The state has lifted a "boil water" advisory for residents in Bluffview after sampling done this week showed the water supply is safe.
Bluffview is a small residential area on U.S. 12 south of Baraboo, across from the old Badger Army Ammunition plant.
The advisory was issued on July 8 by the Department of Natural Resources after coliform bacteria was found in the water.
The advisory was rescinded on Thursday after a second round of safe water samples were reported to the DNR by the State Laboratory of Hygiene in Madison.
"Two rounds of three samples were collected this week from the distribution system and all samples were reported to be safe," DNR water supply engineer Dave Barkhahn of Horicon said in a news release.
"It appears that chlorination was effective in eliminating the coliform bacteria from the water system," Barkhahn said. "Three more samples will be collected next week."
During the advisory, all residents in Bluffview were advised to boil their water prior to drinking or preparing food, or to use commercially bottled water.
A water sample collected July 1 indicated the presence of coliform bacteria. Further sampling July 6 confirmed the presence. While coliform bacteria, which are naturally present in the environment, are not generally harmful themselves, they are an indicator that other, potentially harmful bacteria may be present.
Posted in Local, Environment on Friday, July 16, 2010 7:05 am Updated: 7:07 am

Environment Department Issues 'Boil Water Advisory' for Socorro Water System Customers are urged to Boil Water Prior to Drinking
Targeted News Service
July 16, 2010 Friday 2:20 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 305 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau has issued a "boil water advisory for the Socorro Water System.
NMED issued the advisory today after bacteriological contamination was discovered in one of the drinking water sources for the Socorro Water System. NMED requires the Socorro Water System to notify water consumers of the finding. This advisory only applies to the drinking water at the Socorro Water System, and does not extend to any of the other surrounding water systems.
Consumers of water at the Socorro Water System are advised to boil the water for five minutes before drinking, cooking, dishwashing and bathing. The presence of E. coli in water indicates that the water may have been in contact with sewage or animal wastes, and could contain disease-causing organisms. Most strains of E. coli are harmless and live in the intestines of healthy humans and animals. However, a positive test for E. coli in the drinking water supply may indicate the presence of dangerous strains of E. coli or other disease-causing organisms. These types of organisms may cause severe gastrointestinal illness and, in rare cases, death. Children, the elderly and immuno-compromised individuals are at an increased risk for illness.
The NMED Drinking Water Bureau will provide technical assistance to the water system and will test the water until no further threat of contamination remains.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Mike Huber, Drinking Water Bureau Compliance Manager, at (505) 660-3834.
Contact: Marissa Stone Bardino, NMED Communications Director, 505/827-0314, 505/231-0475

Man dies after bridge fall during Ky. flash floods
The Associated Press
July 18, 2010 Sunday 06:50 PM GMT


Copyright 2010 Associated Press All Rights Reserved
Section: DOMESTIC NEWS
Length: 116 words
Dateline: PIKEVILLE, Ky.
Body


Kentucky State Police say a man who was checking on a relative's home during flash flooding was killed when he fell from a bridge.
Police said in a press release that Craig Morris of Carrie had stopped on a highway bridge Saturday in Zebulon in eastern Kentucky. He was looking out over the area when he fell to his death.
Emergency officials say numerous homes were damaged, some were washed away, and roads and bridges were damaged during the flash flooding Saturday.
The Lexington Herald-Leader reports that homes throughout the central part of the county were without tap water and would be on a boil-water advisory when it comes back on. The storms also knocked out power to hundreds of customers.

Environment Department Lifts 'Boil Water Advisory' for Socorro Water System
Targeted News Service
July 19, 2010 Monday 2:16 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 349 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau is lifting a "boil water advisory" for the Socorro Water System.
NMED issued the advisory on July 16, 2010 after bacteriological contamination (E. coli) was discovered in one of the drinking water sources for the Socorro Water System. NMED required the Socorro Water System to notify water consumers of the finding. This advisory only applied to the drinking water at the Socorro Water System, and did not extend to any of the other surrounding water systems.
Consumers of water at the Socorro Water System were advised to boil the water for five minutes before drinking, cooking, dishwashing and bathing. The presence of E. coli in water indicates that the water may have been in contact with sewage or animal wastes, and could contain disease-causing organisms. Most strains of E. coli are harmless and live in the intestines of healthy humans and animals. However, a positive test for E. coli in the drinking water supply may indicate the presence of dangerous strains of E. coli or other disease-causing organisms. These types of organisms may cause severe gastrointestinal illness and, in rare cases, death. Children, the elderly and immuno-compromised individuals are at an increased risk for illness.
The NMED Drinking Water Bureau provided technical assistance to the water system and determined that adequate disinfection (chlorination) is provided at a level that mitigates the potential threat to public health. The Socorro Water System will maintain a regular monitoring schedule to ensure adequate levels of disinfection, and continue to test the distribution system for the presence of E. coli.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Mike Huber, Drinking Water Bureau Compliance Manager, at (505) 660-3834.
Contact: Marissa Stone Bardino, NMED Communications Director, 505/827-0314, 505/231-0475

Boil Water Order Lifted as of Noon Monday
Targeted News Service
July 19, 2010 Monday 11:10 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 374 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SOCORRO, N.M.
Body


New Mexico Institute of Mining & Technology issued the following news release:
After extensive monitoring of the City of Socorro water supply, the state Environmental Department lifted the boil water order at noon Monday.
The state Environmental Department on Saturday, July 17, instructed the City of Socorro to issue a "boil water order" after E. coli was found at the Sedillo Spring well.
E. Coli is a bacterium that can cause food poisoning in humans. E. Coli was found during regular testing at the water source Sedillo Spring, which is one of five water sources used by the City of Socorro.
For the KRQE news report, click here (http://www.krqe.com/dpp/news/health/city-heeds-e-coli-contamination-warning).
For the local report in the Defensor Chieftain, click here (http://www.dchieftain.com/dc/index.php/news/1751-boil-water-advisory.html).
Further testing showed no E. coli in the domestic water distribution system; however, the City has issued a boil water order for the entire town until the source tests clean.
Consumers of water at the Socorro Water System are advised to boil the water for five minutes before drinking, cooking, dishwashing and bathing. Most strains of E. coli are harmless and live in the intestines of healthy humans and animals. However, a positive test for E. coli in the drinking water supply may indicate the presence of dangerous strains of E. coli or other disease-causing organisms. These types of organisms may cause severe gastrointestinal illness and, in rare cases, death. Children, the elderly and immuno-compromised individuals are at an increased risk for illness.
Jim McLain, assistant director of Facilities Management at Tech, said the west and north sides of campus draw water from sources other than Sedillo Spring. The south side of the main campus draws water from Sedillo Spring.
The NMED Drinking Water Bureau will provide technical assistance to the water system and will test the water until no further threat of contamination remains.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Mike Huber, Drinking Water Bureau Compliance Manager, at (505) 660-3834.

Gov. Beshear Meets with Pike County Officials Following Flooding
Targeted News Service
July 19, 2010 Monday 10:14 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 620 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: FRANKFORT, Ky.
Body


Gov. Steve Beshear, D-Ky., issued the following news release:
Governor Steve Beshear visited areas of Pike County today following weekend storms that caused severe flooding and mudslides. The storms are blamed for two deaths in Pike County.
"I have seen startling and significant damage in Pike County today," said Gov. Beshear. "My administration, from Emergency Management to the Transportation Cabinet and beyond, is working quickly to get these struggling Kentucky families the help they need."
Gov. Beshear's trip included stops at Raccoon Creek and a meeting with local officials at the Pike County Courthouse. Gov. Beshear declared a State of Emergency on Sunday for Pike and Shelby counties and requested Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) to conduct preliminary damage assessments. Seven FEMA assessment teams will begin work tomorrow.
"My heart goes out to the hundreds of families impacted by this torrential flooding. I want to assure the people of Pike County that help is on the way and we will utilize every resource to help those paralyzed by this natural disaster," said Congressman Hal Rogers. "I applaud the Governor for declaring a state of emergency and as necessary, I will be working with officials here in Washington to make sure that things are moving as quickly as possible to bring temporary relief while we begin the rebuilding process. While more challenges lie ahead, I know the resilient people of Pike County and together we will overcome this tragedy and become a stronger community."
Up to eight inches of rain fell in a short period of time, prompting emergency evacuations and rescues. Pike Co. Emergency Management officials estimate approximately 200 homes were damaged or destroyed by the weekend's flooding and mudslides.
"It looks more like a tornado has been through here than a flood in some places," said Pike County Judge Executive Wayne T. Rutherford. "This is the most devastating flood I have ever seen. But we are resilient in these mountains and we will pull through it."
Approximately 400 residents remain without power in Pike County, down from more than 7,000 Sunday. Approximately 13,500 residents are without water, and another 13,000 are under a boil water advisory. Water distribution points will operate until restoration is complete. One shelter remains open at Pike Central High School, where 25 people stayed Sunday night. The Kentucky Community Crises Response Board (KCCRB) sent a counseling team to the area on Sunday and is expected to have expanded teams in the county beginning today.
Safety Tips
* Kentuckians are encouraged to monitor river and streams crests for their areas and heed warnings or evacuation orders from local officials. Do not drive through or wade through any water, no matter if just a few inches. STOP, TURN AROUND - DON'T DROWN!
* Do not attempt to enter flooded structures unless a certified electrician has shut the power off.
* Be aware of toxic or hazardous wastes associated with flood waters. For additional information on health safety tips and flood water clean-up, please visit the Department for Public Health's website at www.chfs.ky.gov/dph/.
* For statewide road conditions please visit www.511.ky.gov .
* For local information and or shelter locations, please contact your local emergency management office. Follow this link for assistance: http://www.kyem.ky.gov/about/countyemdirectors.htm .
* For river levels and expected crests, visit http://water.weather.gov/ahps/ and click on the area you wish to observe.
* For additional information on this and other Kentucky disasters, please visit www.kyem.ky.gov .
Contact: Kerri Richardson, 502/564-2611
Copyright Targeted News Services
TNS C-BhaS 100720-mv45-2920226 61MarlynVitin

Damage Assessment Teams Begin Work in Pike County
Targeted News Service
July 20, 2010 Tuesday 3:29 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 629 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: FRANKFORT, Ky.
Body


Gov. Steve Beshear, D-Ky., issued the following news release:
Through a coordinated joint effort, Preliminary Damage Assessment (PDA) teams consisting of personnel from local, state and federal government have begun gathering damage estimates from local government and private citizens in Pike County.
"The aftermath of the flooding in Pike County is really unlike anything I've seen before," said Gov. Beshear, who visited the area yesterday to meet with local officials. "Swiftly moving water is extremely dangerous and its ability to cause destruction should never be underestimated."
Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) personnel arrived in Pike County yesterday. After being briefed by local and Kentucky Division of Emergency Management (KYEM) officials, teams were assembled and county assessments were assigned. These teams will begin PDAs throughout the county today. These damage assessments will be used to support Gov. Beshear's request for federal assistance.
"We are hoping to expedite the assistance process by having the FEMA teams conduct these damage assessments with our local teams," said John Heltzel, director for KYEM. "We want to bring whatever assistance is needed, and eligible, to all of Pike County and its residents as soon as possible."
Officials encourage those who have suffered property damage to photograph the damage, save any repair receipts and report your damage to the local emergency management director.
The Kentucky National Guard currently has 24 Soldiers on duty providing support to Pike County. For the past several days, members of the 577th Sapper Company, 201st Engineer Battalion have conducted security patrols in humvees in support of local law enforcement, and UH-60 Black Hawk helicopter crews have assisted in damage assessment. Additional troops from the 201st are being brought on to provide communications and logistical support in the distribution of bottled water.
If you do not have the family and/or financial resources to clean out your property, you can call 606-432-0210 to request volunteer assistance. "Folks need to be aware volunteer groups are available to help clean up they cannot dismantle or remove destroyed homes," said Jim Garrett, Voluntary Agency Liaison for Volunteer Organizations Active in Disaster (VOAD).
Safety Messages:
* Do not drive through or wade through any water, no matter if it's just a few inches. STOP - TURN AROUND - DON'T DROWN!
* The Kentucky Division of Water (DOW) reports that boil water advisories are in effect for much of the county due to broken lines and other factors. Water distribution points have been established to assist those without water. Check with your local government for current water distribution locations.
* DOW also warns against contact with floodwaters due to contamination from sewage, agricultural products and other harmful substances.
* The Kentucky Department of Public Health (DPH) encourages flooded residents to be aware of toxic or hazardous wastes associated with flood waters. For additional information on health safety tips and flood water clean-up, please visit the DPH's website at www.chfs.ky.gov/dph/ or contact the local health department.
* Do not attempt to enter flooded structures unless a certified electrician has shut the power off.
* Avoid unnecessary sight seeing, keeping the roadways clear and allowing emergency officials access to the impacted areas.
For local information and/or shelter locations, please contact your local emergency management office. Follow this link for assistance: http://www.kyem.ky.gov/about/countyemdirectors.htm .
For additional information, visit the KyEM website at www.kyem.ky.gov.
Contact: Kerri Richardson, 502/564-2611

V.I. now sending out emergency alerts online and by phone
The Virgin Islands Daily News, St. Thomas
July 20, 2010 Tuesday


Copyright 2010 The Virgin Islands Daily News
Distributed by McClatchy-Tribune Business News
Section: STATE AND REGIONAL NEWS
Length: 825 words
Byline: Constance Cooper, The Virgin Islands Daily News, St. Thomas
Body


July 20--ST. THOMAS -- If a tsunami, hurricane or any other natural disaster is headed toward the territory, now anyone can be alerted to the situation within seconds after those who monitor such things find out themselves.
In a news conference Monday, the V.I. Territorial Emergency Management Agency announced the launch of VI-Alert, a system that sends disaster alerts directly to the public.
By signing up at VITEMA's website, www.vitema.gov, Virgin Islanders can choose how they want to be notified of the threat -- via a text message, a phone call, a fax, an e-mail, page, RSS feed or even Twitter.
"This system was chosen realizing that today's citizens are increasingly relying on modern communications technologies as their information sources -- cell phones, PDAs, Internet -- whereas most traditional emergency alert systems provide alerts by television and broadcast radio systems," Gov. Jongh deJongh Jr. said at the news conference.
But traditional alert systems will not be left out, and neither will people who don't have Internet access. VI-Alert allows users to set up notifications for family members and friends who are not online, and television, radio and other media outlets can sign up for Common Alerting Protocol notifications -- a standardized warning system used to disseminate the same warnings, the same way, over local, regional and national outlets.
Additionally, VITEMA Director Mark Walters announced Monday that his agency has selected a contractor to install a siren system in the territory to warn residents of weather threats. Walters declined to name the contractor selected or the cost of the project, until negotiations are complete, but he said that alarms will be funded with federal Homeland Security grants.
Walter said he hopes to have the sirens -- which will be tied to VI-Alert -- in place by the end of hurricane season.
VITEMA started working on VI-Alert in March, when a high-level team of Virgin Islands emergency responders sat down and, as an exercise, tried to figure out how they would notify the public if there was a disaster at one of the V.I. Water and Power Authority's power plants.
"We realized that we had a significant shortfall in our ability to reach out to the public in a quick and timely manner," Walters said.
So, Walters turned to the Federal Emergency Management Agency, which is, technically, still his employer. Walters is on loan from FEMA's New York offices, where he is the Region II director of Mission Support, and FEMA pays his salary while he is serving as VITEMA director.
VI-Alert taps into the New York state's $13 million emergency notification system. VITEMA has paid $40,000 in start-up costs to link into New York's system, and will pay $20,000 per year in maintenance costs after the first year.
For those who sign up to receive them, earthquake alerts will be sent directly from the U.S. Geological Survey; tsunami alerts will come straight from the Alaska Tsunami Warning Center; and severe weather notices will be issued directly from the National Weather Service.
Other warnings will be written by VITEMA, then sent out to the public.
Currently, VI-Alert is equipped to offer severe weather alerts; earthquake and tsunami alerts; beach closings; and public health alerts, such as boil-water advisories.
Walters said that he is in discussion with other government agencies to add other bulletins, including those for a missing child notifications, an escaped prisoner or a gunman at large.
VITEMA also is working with the territory's public and private schools, as well as the University of the Virgin Islands, to sign up students for school-specific alerts.
Kevin Ross, assistant IT director of the New York State Emergency Management Office, who developed New York's alert system, said he is in talks with cruise ship companies to obtain copies of their ships manifest, so cruise passengers can be signed up for VI-Alert while they are in port. The passengers' contact information would be automatically deleted from the system once they leave the Virgin Islands, Ross said.
In October, New York will roll out a new version of the system, which will include applications for iPhones, Blackberries, Droids, Windows Mobile Devices and personal computers. A VI-Alert version of the applications will come out simultaneously, Ross said.
The updated version also will have Spanish language capabilities, and Walters said a Spanish-speaking VITEMA employee will translate the warnings.
To see more of The Virgin Islands Daily News, or to subscribe to the newspaper, go to http://www.virginislandsdailynews.com/. Copyright (c) 2010, The Virgin Islands Daily News, St. Thomas Distributed by McClatchy-Tribune Information Services. For more information about the content services offered by McClatchy-Tribune Information Services (MCT), visit   www.mctinfoservices.com, e-mail services@mctinfoservices.com, or call 866-280-5210 (outside the United States, call +1 312-222-4544).

Penn Will Cut Water Bills
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
July 21, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 7
Length: 311 words
Byline: Civia Katz, Correspondent
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


BY CIVIA KATZ
Correspondent
Penn Township is rebating water costs to residents placed under a boil water advisory for nearly three weeks that ended July 13.
About 575 water customers will receive a 25 percent discount on their water bills.
"We will prorate your water bills for the 22 days. We will adjust the bills so your water bills will be discounted," Dave Sarley, supervisor chairman, said July 12.
The township issued a boil water advisory when a parasite, cryptosporidium, was found in the water supply. At the time, the township water was not filtered. It was treated with chlorine, which cryptosporidium is resistant to.
Cryptosporidium causes intestinal symptoms, especially in people who have a suppressed immune system.
Township Manager Dave Kratzer said July 12 that the township had received no reports of illness.
The township brought in a portable system July 2 at a cost of $25,000 a month. The rented unit will filter the water until a permanent system is built sometime in 2011. Kratzer said the township will not be passing on these costs to the residents.
Public water users were without water for a period of 45 minutes during the boil water advisory. In an e-mail dated July 16, Kratzer said the outage occurred July 11 and was caused by an electrical issue with a motor.
The interconnection that the township tried with the Manheim Borough Water Authority did not provide adequate pressure to supply water to higher elevations of the water system. As a result, Kratzer said, the water storage tank went offline.
The future filtration plant will cost the township about $3 million. It will filter out bacteria and also address the nitrate issues the township has had with the public water.
The township had two high nitrate readings in February, which triggered the need for a feasibility study required by the state Department of Environmental Protection.

GOV. BESHEAR DECLARES STATE OF EMERGENCY FOLLOWING STORMS AND FLOODING
States News Service
July 21, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 710 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: FRANKFORT, KY
Body


The following information was released by the office of the governor of Kentucky:
Governor Steve Beshear today declared a State of Emergency in Kentucky following severe storms that struck Pike and Shelby counties early Sunday morning and several northeastern Kentuckian counties late Tuesday night and early Wednesday morning. The storms have caused flash flooding, evacuations and water rescues in the northeastern Kentucky counties of Carter, Elliott, Lewis, Mason and Rowan counties. Those counties have each declared states of emergency; the cities of Olive Hill and Maysville have also declared local states of emergency.
Gov. Beshear also signed an executive order today to trigger the price gouging statutes that protect consumers from unscrupulous businesses that attempt to artificially inflate prices as a result of the emergency.
The executive order will allow for investigation into any complaints of price gouging that may occur relative to gas, heating, building supplies, hotels and other goods and services in the aftermath of the weekend's storms.
Weather reports indicate as much as six inches of rain has fallen on parts of northeast Kentucky. The Little Sandy River is rising and expected to crest above flood stage in Grayson. American Electric Power reports approximately 566 customers in Letcher, Carter and Lewis counties are currently without power. Approximately 400 Lewis County homes are currently without water.
In Carter County, a shelter operated by the Salvation Army has opened at Grahn Community Center. Early estimates indicate that 50 to 60 homes in Carter County were affected by the floods, approximately 20 of which are destroyed. Eight roads are currently underwater in Fleming County. KY-57 is closed at the Fleming-Lewis county line and multiple roads are closed in the Laurel Camp Dix area in Lewis County. Forty homes in Rowan County have been flooded, two of which have been destroyed. At least 100 cars were flooded, and 20 county bridges and 20 private bridges with approaches have been washed out.
Officials expect the amount of damages to increase as water recedes in the impacted counties, as emergency workers and local officials will be able to reach areas previously under water and hope to have a better assessment on the extent of damage.
These latest floods came just days after heavy thunderstorms hit Pike and Shelby counties. Two fatalities are attributed to the Pike County storms. Gov. Steve Beshear declared states of emergency for both counties over the weekend. Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) assessment teams have been working to evaluate damages in Pike County for two days, which will expedite the process for applying for any applicable federal assistance.
Pike County updates
Local, state and federal damage assessment teams continue assessing the property damage in Pike County.
In Pike County, 2,400 residents remain without water and much of the county remains on boil water advisories. Volunteers are taking drinking water to impacted areas, and water distribution points have been established throughout the county. Three shelters are open in the area.
Safety Tips
Kentuckians are encouraged to monitor weather (www.weather.com) for their areas and heed warnings or evacuation orders from local officials. Do not drive through or wade through any water, no matter if just a few inches. STOP, TURN AROUND DON'T DROWN!
Do not attempt to enter flooded structures unless a certified electrician has shut off the power.
For additional information and safety tips, please visit KyEM's website at www.kyem.ky.gov.
Be aware of toxic or hazardous wastes associated with flood waters. For additional information on health safety tips and flood water clean-up, please visit the Department for Public Health's website at www.chfs.ky.gov/dph/.
For statewide road conditions please visit www.511.ky.gov .
For local information and or shelter locations, please contact your local emergency management office. Follow this link for assistance: http://www.kyem.ky.gov/about/countyemdirectors.htm .
For river levels and expected crests, visit http://water.weather.gov/ahps/ and click on the area you wish to observe.
For additional information on this and other Kentucky disasters, please visit www.kyem.ky.gov .

Load-Date: July 22, 2010


End of Document

Environment Department Issues 'Boil Water Advisory' for El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System
Targeted News Service
July 23, 2010 Friday 2:13 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 382 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau has issued a "boil water advisory" for the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System.
NMED issued the advisory on July 23, 2010 after bacteriological contamination that exceeded the Maximum Contaminant Level for E. coli was discovered in drinking water at the water system. NMED requires the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association to notify water consumers of the finding. The El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System is located approximately 20 miles south of Santa Fe. This advisory only applies to customers served by the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association, and does not extend to any of the other surrounding water systems or communities.
Consumers of water at the El Vadito de Los Cerrillos Water Association Water System are advised to boil the water for five minutes before drinking, cooking, dishwashing and bathing. The presence of E. coli in water indicates that the water may have been in contact with sewage or animal wastes, and could contain disease-causing organisms. Most strains of E. coli are harmless and live in the intestines of healthy humans and animals. However, a positive test for E. coli in the drinking water supply may indicate the presence of dangerous strains of E. coli or other disease-causing organisms. These types of organisms may cause severe gastrointestinal illness and, in rare cases, death. Children, the elderly and immuno-compromised individuals are at an increased risk for illness.
Actions have been initiated to disinfect the water system and identify possible sources of contamination, establish acceptable disinfection, and flush out the water system. The NMED Drinking Water Bureau will provide technical assistance to the water system and will test the water until no further threat of contamination remains.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Mike Huber, Drinking Water Bureau Compliance Manager, at (505) 660-3834.
Contact: Marissa Stone Bardino, NMED Communications Director, 505/827-0314, 505/231-0475
Copyright Targeted News Services
TNS hc11-JF78100726-2928208 StaffFurigay

BRIEF: Boil-water advisory issued for part of Ironton: Advisory is for Eighth Street from Washington to Adams streets
The Ironton Tribune, Ohio
July 26, 2010 Monday


Copyright 2010 The Ironton Tribune, Ohio
Distributed by McClatchy-Tribune Business News
Section: STATE AND REGIONAL NEWS
Length: 163 words
Byline: Lori Kersey, The Ironton Tribune, Ohio
Body


July 26--IRONTON -- Residents on one block in Ironton should continue until tomorrow to boil their water before drinking it.
A cautionary boil-water advisory was issued for residents of Eighth Street from Washington to Adams Street because of a water main break that occurred around 4 a.m. Sunday, said Steve Collins, water plant operator for the City of Ironton.
"Anytime you shut the water off you have to put out an advisory," Collins said.
The water will be tested and the advisory should be lifted Tuesday, he said.

Damage Assessments Continuing in Hard Hit Counties
Targeted News Service
July 26, 2010 Monday 11:59 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 604 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: FRANKFORT, Ky.
Body


Gov. Steve Beshear, D-Ky., issued the following news release:
Gov. Steve Beshear today said that local emergency management officials continue conducting damage assessments from last week's devastating storms, which caused severe flooding in several northeastern Kentucky counties.
Gov. Beshear was notified late Friday afternoon that President Barack Obama approved his request for a major disaster declaration for Pike County for assistance from the severe storms and flooding that hit Saturday, July 17, causing two fatalities and severe damage across the county. This presidential declaration came just two days after the Governor made his request to the president for federal assistance.
"I am extremely pleased that we were able to validate the damage, submit the request and be awarded federal assistance so quickly," said Gov. Beshear. "I am also pleased that as soon as other counties hit the eligibility thresholds we will be able to add them to the existing presidential major disaster declaration. Not having to submit separate requests for each impacted county will greatly expedite the delivery of necessary federal assistance."
Shelby County was also hard hit by storms on July 17, and damage assessments are underway. Carter, Elliot, Lawrence, Lewis, Mason and Rowan counties declared state of emergencies due to severe flooding on July 20 and 21 and damage assessments are continuing in those counties. If those counties reach the required damage threshold, they will be added to the President's major disaster declaration. Approximately 2,225 customers remain on boiled water advisories in these northeastern Kentucky counties.
Details of the Pike County Disaster Declaration, KY-1925
July 23 - President Obama granted federal disaster assistance for both Individual Assistance (IA) and Public Assistance (PA) for Pike County:
* The President's action makes federal funding available to affected individuals in Pike County.
* Assistance can include grants for temporary housing and home repairs, low-cost loans to cover uninsured property losses and other programs to help individuals and business owners recover from the effects of the disaster.
* Federal funding also is available to the state and eligible local governments and certain private nonprofit organizations on a cost-sharing basis for emergency work and the repair or replacement of facilities damaged by the severe storms, flooding and mudslides in Pike County.
* Federal funding is also available on a cost-sharing basis for hazard mitigation measures statewide.
* Pike County residents and business owners who sustained losses can begin applying for assistance by registering online at www.DisasterAssistance.gov or by calling 1-800-621-FEMA (3362) or 1-800-462-7585 (TTY) for the hearing and speech impaired. The toll-free telephone numbers will operate from 7 a.m. to 10 p.m. (local time). Residents MUST register with FEMA to be eligible for assistance.
* Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) Mobile Disaster Recovery Centers opened earlier today in Pike County at two locations: in the lower parking lot of Pikeville/Pike County Community Funeral Home located on Zebulon Highway and the second location is at the mouth of Harlesses' Creek on US Hwy 460 at Community Bank.
* Approximately 25,000 Pike County customers remain on boiled water advisories and 75 residents on Harlesses' Creek are without water.
For additional disaster recovery information, including FEMA assistance programs, visit the KyEM website at www.kyem.ky.gov.
Contact: Kerri Richardson, 502/564-2611
Copyright Targeted News Services

Expert Joins Penn Water Authority
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
August 4, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 6
Length: 296 words
Byline: Civia Katz, Correspondent
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


BY CIVIA KATZ
Correspondent
Penn Township approved the appointment of resident Charles Smith to the Northwestern Lancaster County Authority at the July 12 supervisors meeting.
Smith, an expert on cryptosporidium, offered his services when the parasite was found in the public water system in June. "This is one of the more positive things that came out of the water crisis," Dave Sarley, supervisor chairman, said. "He's an expert on all these little bugs."
Smith is a certified water technologist. He said only 400 people hold this certification nationally, and it represents the highest credential in the industrial and commercial water treatment field. Smith was one of the first 60 people to receive the certification. Exam requirements exam include five years of experience investigating water treatment problems and implementing corrective action.
"He has impeccable credentials," Sarley said. "With his knowledge of cryptosporidium, I said I got to have this guy. We're happy to have you."
When the parasite was found in the water, the township issued a boil water advisory. Smith told supervisors and about 20 residents at the meeting the parasite is a macro organism that can be filtered out of the water system. It is a hardy parasite that is encapsulated, protecting it from chemicals like chlorine.
"Cryptosporidium has to complete its life cycle. It needs a warm host to complete its cycle," Smith said. Without a host, the cryptosporidium cannot reproduce, and it is not harmful, he said.
Mike Wolgemuth of Severn Trent, the firm that oversees the water treatment, said eight cryptosporidium were found in the water. Since July 2, the township water has used a temporary water filtration system that will be operational until a permanent filtering plant is built next year.

Environment Department Lifts 'Boil Water Advisory' for Tajique MDWCA in Torrance County
Targeted News Service
August 5, 2010 Thursday 3:33 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 247 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau is lifting a "boil water advisory" for the Tajique Mutual Domestic Water Consumers Association on the east side of the Manzano Mountains in Torrance County.
NMED issued the advisory on April 21 due to multiple failures by the Tajique MDWCA to test for bacteria in the drinking water as required by the New Mexico Drinking Water Regulations. The association, which is a small community water system, serves approximately 180 people. NMED required the Tajique MDWCA to notify its customers and members that the water system was not meeting the water sampling and reporting requirements. While there was no indication of contamination of the drinking water, without bacteria water sample results NMED could not be certain of the safety of the water provided by the Tajique MDWCA.
Subsequent water quality samples have shown no bacteriological contamination of the water system. These clean results have allowed NMED's Drinking Water Bureau to lift the "boil water advisory" for the Tajique MDWCA.
For more information, call NMED Communications Director Marissa Stone Bardino at (505) 827-0314 or (505) 231-0475 or Mike Huber, Drinking Water Bureau Compliance Manager, at (505) 660-3834.
Contact: Marissa Stone Bardino, NMED Communications Director, 505/827-0314, 505/231-0475

No boil advisory following break in city water line
Republican & Herald (Pottsville, Pennsylvania)
August 5, 2010 Thursday


Copyright 2010 Republican & Herald
Distributed by McClatchy-Tribune Business News
Section: STATE AND REGIONAL NEWS
Length: 340 words
Byline: Amanda Leigh Brozana, Republican and Herald, Pottsville, Pa.
Body


Aug. 05--A contractor working on a construction project near Tunnel Road outside Pottsville broke a water line Wednesday morning causing discoloration.
Patrick M. Caulfield, director of the Schuylkill Municipal Authority, said a water boil advisory was not put in effect. He said he expected the issue to clear up on its own.
Caulfield said the break occurred about 9 a.m.
"They contacted us immediately and within minutes we had someone on site able to isolate the break up and down stream and close valves," Caulfield said. "We were still able to keep pressure in all the pipes and water in all the pipes."
The discoloration, Caulfield said, was due to the fact that scaling built up inside the pipe is scuffed away due to the velocity of water surging through the pipe after the break.
"However, there's no contamination, therefore, we are not required to issue a boil water advisory," Caulfield said.
Caulfield said the area where the line was broken is a place where there is redundant line, making it easier to quickly target the problem and make sure customers were not greatly affected.
Roma Pizza, 116 W. Market St., was using 2-liter Coke products instead of fountain soda while the water ran with a brown tint. Hong Kong Buffet, 118 E. Norwegian St., closed its doors Wednesday until the water cleared.
Wendy's on Route 61 North, near the Fairlane Village mall, had a sign posted on the drive-through menu indicating they were closed due to a water problem.
Nearby, McDonald's had suspended serving fountain drinks while the water problem was being addressed.

Targeted News Service
August 13, 2010 Friday 2:42 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 229 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANTA FE, N.M.
Body


The New Mexico Department of the Environment issued the following news release:
The New Mexico Environment Department's Drinking Water Bureau is lifting a "boil water advisory" for the Tecolote Mutual Domestic Water Consumers Association (MDWCA)Water System.
NMED issued the advisory on August 2, 2010 after bacteriological contamination that exceeded the Maximum Contaminant Level for E. coli was discovered in the water system. NMED required the Tecolote Water System to notify all water consumers of the finding.
Corrective actions were taken by the water system, including disinfecting the water system by increasing the level of chlorination and identifying possible sources of contamination. Consumers were advised to boil all water prior to ingestion.
Water samples collected since the corrective actions were taken have shown no E. coli present in the water system. These clean results have allowed NMED's Drinking Water Bureau to advise the Tecolote MDWCA Water System to lift the "boil water advisory" for the water system.

Two more water main breaks were later identified bringing the total to eight water main breaks that have drained Ames water towers to dangerously low levels. Akron Issues Boil Water Advisory
Intelligencer Journal/New Era (Lancaster, Pennsylvania)
August 14, 2010 Saturday


Copyright 2010 Lancaster Newspapers, Inc.
Section: B; Pg. 2
Length: 209 words
Byline: Diana Martin
Dateline: Lancaster, PA
Body


Residents in Akron Borough are urged to boil water after a well tested positive for E. coli Thursday.
Bacteria was found in one of the borough's eight public wells. The well has been taken off-line and the plant is increasing chlorination and flushing out the system.
The area's 4,000 residents have been put on a boil-water advisory until further notice. The problem is anticipated to be resolved by Friday, Mayor John McBeth said.
E. coli are bacteria whose presence indicates that the water may be contaminated with human or animal wastes, the advisory stated.
Microbes in these wastes can cause diarrhea, cramps, nausea, headaches, or other symptoms. They may pose a special health risk for infants, young children, some of the elderly and people with severely compromised immune systems.
"Drink boiled or bottled," reminded McBeth.
Boiled water should also be used for making ice, brushing teeth, washing dishes and food preparation.
In July, water in Penn Township tested positive for the parasite cryptosporidium. Residents were put on a 3-week boil-water advisory.
Since July 2, the township has been using a temporary water filtration system. A permanent water filtration system will be built next year, at an estimated cost of $3 million.
dmartin@lnpnews.com

Boil Water Advisory Remains in Effect; Water Volume Restrictions to be Lifted
Targeted News Service
August 14, 2010 Saturday 9:59 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 428 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: AMES, Iowa
Body


The city of Ames issued the following news release:
As flushing efforts conclude, the City of Ames' Water Department has announced that the water volume restrictions will be lifted as of 2 p.m. today, including restrictions on exterior water use. Ames citizens will be able to resume their normal water usage, including laundry, toilet flushing, showers/bathing and outdoor debris clean-up. The boil advisory will remain in effect for Ames citizens until further notice.
"We have made tremendous progress," said John Dunn, director of the City's Water and Pollution Control Department. "We are progressing better than I dared to hope, but we ask that the public please continue their conservation efforts and don't start using mass amounts of water prior to 2 p.m., as we need to allow the water towers to fill up again."
Dunn said that crews did respond to a four-inch water main break last night along Murray Drive but repairs were completed by 11 p.m.
Ames citizens are reminded that while the volume restrictions will be lifted, the water is still not safe for human consumption. Water coming from the tap should still not be used for purposes such as drinking, brushing teeth, washing dishes, preparing food, and making ice, unless boiled or treated first. Both commercial and residential dishwashers are also not considered effective means of sanitizing the water.
So far, 88 water samples have been collected by the Water and Pollution Control Department, with 90 more water samples scheduled to be collected today.
Safe drinking water will continue to be distributed at all four locations in Ames until the boil advisory is lifted. These sites include Sam's Club on Airport Road, McFarland Clinic West (next to West HyVee), ISU Towers parking lot, and Wal-Mart on Grand Avenue. Residents may pick up two gallons of water per person each day.
As of 6:00 Saturday morning, water readings for Squaw Creek and the Skunk River were:
* Squaw Creek at Lincoln Way: 4.6 feet
* Skunk River at Riverside Drive: 8.73 feet
* Skunk River at U.S. 30: 18.52 feet
"Health and safety have been, and will continue to be, our main focus," said Mayor Ann Campbell. "The community's response and cooperation is greatly appreciated."
All roads in Ames are now open but drivers are asked to use caution, as there may be debris in some locations.
A 4 p.m. press conference is scheduled for Sunday, August 15, in the council chambers, for further flood updates.

Boil Advisory Issued for Shady Valley Mobile Home Park
Targeted News Service
August 19, 2010 Thursday 7:01 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 216 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: OKLAHOMA CITY
Body


The Oklahoma Department of Environmental Quality issued the following news release:
The Oklahoma Department of Environmental Quality (DEQ) has advised Shady Valley Mobile Home Park, located in Pottawatomie County, to inform consumers of the drinking water that it is unsafe for human consumption due to the presence of E. coli.
The boil advisory was issued after water samples indicated the presence of E. coli. To ensure the water is safe for human consumption, water served from the Shady Valley Mobile Home Park system should be vigorously boiled for at least one minute before drinking, use in food preparation, washing dishes or brushing teeth.
The advisory to boil water will remain in effect until the water system ensures that chlorination can be adequately maintained and that, if necessary, any required corrections to structural systems or operational practices have been made. DEQ will require that proper testing of water samples indicates the water to be free from E. coli before suspending this advisory.
Federal law requires that consumers be notified when a public water supply exceeds certain maximum contaminant levels and might be harmful to the health of consumers.

Body


ST. THOMAS, Ont. - A boil water advisory has been issued for residents in parts of southern Ontario.
Officials with Elgin St. Thomas Public Health put out the advisory after a routine water test came back positive for E.coli bacteria.
The advisory was issued for St. Thomas along with portions of Southwold and Central Elgin.
Officials say there have been no reports of illness.
Acting medical officer of health, Dr. Frank Warsh, says they're not sure what the source of the E.coli is or whether it's a sampling error.
The health unit is advising residents to bring their water to a rolling boil for at least one minute prior to using it for drinking, brushing teeth, washing raw foods and making ice. (AM980)

Load-Date: August 21, 2010


End of Document

Byline: CP
Body


(Algae-Toxic-Water)
Public health officials are warning Brockton residents not to use water from two lakes due to potentially harmful toxins from algae.
They say potentially toxic blue-green algae is growing in Marl Lake and Lake Rosalind, north of the town of Hanover.
The municipality includes Walkerton, where tainted water killed seven people in 2000. (The Canadian Press)
(Boil-Water-Advisory)
A positive E.Coli test that prompted a boil water advisory in St. Thomas has turned out to be a false alarm.
The advisory was issued Thursday following lab tests that showed a high level of the bacteria in local water.
But the town's mayor now says those tests were wrong.
The advisory -- which affected about 40-thousand people -- has been lifted. (CKOT)
(Boy-Killed-By-Bus)
Toronto police are seeking witnesses after a 17-year-old boy was struck and killed by a public transit bus.
Police say the boy was hit while crossing the street Friday night.
They say the bus had the green light at the time of the incident. (680 News)
(Manhole-Covers-Stolen)
London police are looking for whoever stole more than a dozen manhole covers in the city.
The thefts began on July 7th and continued until August 18.
A total of 35 manhole covers are missing.
Police say the thefts create a safety issue for pedestrians and drivers. (The Canadian Press)
(Ontario Update by Mary Gazze)
(The Canadian Press)

Body


(BC-Pickton-Report-Bias)
A Vancouver police report on the Robert Pickton investigation says families that tried to file missing persons reports faced ''alleged'' prejudice.
It says some staff members were biased against families of the missing sex workers, but the behaviour of a civilian clerk in the Missing Persons Unit was detrimental to the department.
The report by Deputy Chief Constable Doug LePard says the bias ''poisoned'' the V-P-D's relationship with the families.
LePard says officers are now assigned to deal specifically with sex workers in the Downtown Eastside and forge ties with them. (The Canadian Press)
(BC-Tamil-Protests)
About 100 demonstrators gathered in Vancouver to show support for the Tamil migrants who arrived by ship in B-C earlier this month.
The 500 migrants are being detained while their claims are processed.
The demonstrators in Vancouver, and those at similar rallies across the country, urged authorities to treat the migrants with compassion.
In Toronto, demonstrators draped a banner at an overpass that said ''Tamil Migrants Welcome'' at an overpass.
Rallies organized by a group called ''No one is Illegal'' are planned for later this month in Ottawa, Montreal and Kitchener, Ontario. (CTV, CKNW)
(BC-Boil-Water-Advisory)
White Rock residents are being told to boil their drinking water after E. coli bacteria were discovered in the water treatment system.
The Fraser Health Authority says water should be boiled for at least one minute if it's to be used for drinking, brushing teeth or preparing baby formula.
It says Epcor, the company that runs the treatment plant, hasn't detected the source of the contamination but is flushing the system.
About 80 homes in south Surrey are also affected by the boil water notice. (The Canadian Press)
(BC-Missing-Plane)
Smoke from B-C's wildfires is said to be hindering the search for a missing plane east of Penticton.
The Piper P-A-24 Comanche was carrying four men when it disappeared last Tuesday.
Thick smoke in the area has reduced visibility, and aircraft involved in the search for the Piper are also having to keep a sharp eye out for planes battling the fires.
Friends of the missing men are offering a 10-thousand-dollar reward to anyone who finds them. (Kelowna Daily News)
(BC-Counterattack-Oops)
A 22-year-old man accused of trying evade police at a Counterattack checkpoint in Langley is in serious trouble.
Police say the man drove straight at a Mountie, but the officer was able to jump out of the way just in time.
The vehicle then went through a red light and crashed into a lamp post and a fence.
The driver was later treated for non life-threatening injuries.
Police are recommending he be charged with assault with a weapon, dangerous driving and impaired driving. (The Canadian Press)
(B-C Update by Camille Bains)
(The Canadian Press)

MANITOWANING, Ont. - A boil water advisory for a community on Manitoulin Island has been lifted.
Residents in Manitowaning were ordered to boil their water starting Thursday after the local water treatment plant was hit by lightning.

Boil Water Advisory Rescinded for City of Damar
Targeted News Service
August 27, 2010 Friday 3:37 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 111 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: TOPEKA, Kan.
Body


The Kansas Department of Health and Environment issued the following news release:
The Kansas Department of Health and Environment (KDHE) has rescinded the boil water advisory for the City of Damar, which is located in Rooks County.
KDHE issued the advisory on August 17 due to a line break that resulted in in a loss of pressure to the water distribution system. Laboratory testing on samples collected indicate no evidence of contamination, and all other conditions that place the system at risk of contamination are deemed by KDHE officials to be resolved.

Boil-Water
The Canadian Press - Broadcast Wire
August 28, 2010 Saturday


Copyright 2010 The Canadian Press All Rights Reserved


Section: WESTERN GENERAL NEWS
Length: 148 words
Byline: CP
Body


WHITE ROCK, B.C. - Pigeon droppings are being blamed for a boil water advisory in White Rock that's been extended again throughout the weekend.
The company operating the suburban Vancouver city's water system says it found encapsulated yeast associated with bird feces, potentially the source of e.Coli.
Epcor drained a tank holding 1.2 million litres of water on Wednesday to thoroughly inspect and disinfect it.
Testing continues on potential entry points for the e.Coli, while extensive flushing and sampling of the water distribution system continues.
The company has set up an automatic voice messaging service to call customers and update them on the situation.
Residents are advised to boil any water used for drinking, cooking and brushing teeth for at least one minute, and Epcor says they may notice a slight chlorine odour or discolouration as they fix the problem.
(The Canadian Press)

COWLITZ COUNTY WATER SYSTEM OWNER FACES STIFF STATE FINE
States News Service
September 1, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 358 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
The owner of the Columbia Crest Estates water system in Cowlitz County has been fined $21,060 for violating state health orders to properly maintain the water system and to address ongoing problems with arsenic.
Columbia Crest customers have been under a boil-water advisory since June 2 because owner Dan Class hasn't monitored water quality and doesn't have a certified operator to run the system, as the state requires. The state Department of Health issued the penalty after the failure of attempts to work with Class to address multiple system problems.
The agency's Office of Drinking Water inspected the system in July and found numerous sanitary issues, including mold, algae, and rodent infestations in buildings housing pumps, wells, and storage tanks. In addition, significant leaks pose a contamination risk.
The system serves 22 homes in an unincorporated area between Kalama and Woodland. The Department of Health has reclassified the system's operating permit as "red," which means the system is inadequate. This can affect decisions by local building officials and financial institutions about properties served by this water system.
Class did not comply with state health orders to:
- Hire a professional engineer and submit construction documents for an arsenic removal system to the Department of Health by May 15.
- Hire a certified water system operator by July 13 to run and maintain the system.
- Employ a professional engineer by July 20 to prepare a formal water system plan. These state-mandated plans require owners to demonstrate their technical, managerial and financial ability to maintain a safe and reliable water system.
"He has been given every chance to meet requirements designed to protect the health of his customers," said Clark Halvorson, manager of Southwest operations for the Office of Drinking Water. "We would much rather work cooperatively with water system operators and owners. Unfortunately, in this situation we've had to resort to a fine."
Class has 28 days to appeal the penalty to the agency's Adjudicative Service Unit.

Load-Date: September 2, 2010


End of Document






Boil-Water
The Canadian Press - Broadcast Wire
September 1, 2010 Wednesday


Copyright 2010 The Canadian Press All Rights Reserved


Section: WESTERN GENERAL NEWS
Length: 154 words
Byline: CP
Body


WHITE ROCK, B.C. - People in White Rock, B.C. can drink water directly out of their taps again after officials lifted a boil water advisory that's been in place for 12 days.
About 20,000 people in the city and a small area of Surrey were affected by the advisory, which took effect Aug. 20 after the water became infected with E. coli.
Fraser Health Medical Health Officer Dr. Elizabeth Brodkin says the water is now safe to drink but people are being told to flush out their pipes by running the water for at least a minute before using it.
White Rock's water is not filtered or treated in any way and is provided by a private company called EPCOR, which drained a reservoir holding 1.2 million litres of water to inspect and disinfect it before refilling it.
It's suspected pigeon droppings may have contaminated the water supply.
There are no reports of anyone getting sick as a result of the contamination.
(The Canadian Press)

Load-Date: September 2, 2010

BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR PRUDENCE ISLAND WATER DISTRICT
States News Service
September 3, 2010 Friday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 268 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: PROVIDENCE, RI
Body


The following information was released by the state of Rhode Island:
The Rhode Island Department of Health (HEALTH) has issued a boil water advisory for customers of the Prudence Island Water District (PIWD). HEALTH recommends that water used for bathing of infants, drinking, making ice, brushing teeth or cooking be boiled for one minute and allowed to cool before using. Boiling kills bacteria and other organisms in the water. Bottled water may also be used.
Water system tests confirmed the presence of E. Coli in the public water supply. PIWD is working closely with HEALTH to correct the problem as soon as possible.
The presence of E. Coli bacteria indicates that the water may be contaminated with human or animal wastes. These bacteria can cause diarrhea, cramps, nausea or headaches. Infants, young children, the elderly and anyone with a weakened immune system are at an increased risk for developing more severe symptoms. Consumers who experience any of these symptoms, even if tap water has been avoided, should call their healthcare provider.
This boil water advisory is in effect until further notice from HEALTH. Customers of the Prudence Island Water District are asked to contact neighbors who may not be aware of this advisory.
For information, contact the Prudence Island Water District at 401-835-0475. For general information about drinking water, contact HEALTH's Information Line at 401-222-5960, Monday - Friday, 8:30 a.m. - 4:30 p.m. For information on guidelines for food establishments during and after a boil water advisory, visit http://www.health.ri.gov/environment/dwq/boiladvisory.php

Load-Date: September 3, 2010


End of Document

PRECAUTIONARY BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR MIDDLETOWN WATER CUSTOMERS
States News Service
September 4, 2010 Saturday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 257 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: PROVIDENCE, RI
Body


The following information was released by the state of Rhode Island:
The Rhode Island Department of Health (HEALTH) is issuing a precautionary boil water advisory for Middletown water customers. HEALTH recommends that water being used for drinking, making ice, brushing teeth, cooking, or bathing of infants should be boiled for one minute and allowed to cool before using. Boiling kills bacteria and other organisms in the water. Bottled water can also be used.
Due to a water main break, the water pressure dropped below acceptable limits and therefore, the likelihood for bacterial contamination increases. The water system is working closely with HEALTH to correct the problem as soon as possible.
All water customers in Newport and Middletown are urged to limit water usage to allow the system to restore normal water pressure.
This boil water advisory is in effect until further notice from HEALTH. Middletown water customers are asked to contact neighbors who may not be aware of this advisory.
For information, contact the Station 1 at 845-5826; Julia Forgue at 845-5601; or Ken Mason at 845-5614. For general information about drinking water, contact HEALTH's Information Line at 1-800-942-7434, Monday - Friday, 8:30 a.m. - 4:30 p.m. For information on guidelines for food establishments during and after a boil water advisory, visit http://www.health.ri.gov/environment/dwq/boiladvisory.php

UPDATE ON PRECAUTIONARY BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR MIDDLETOWN WATER CUSTOMERS
States News Service
September 5, 2010 Sunday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 237 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: PROVIDENCE, RI
Body


The following information was released by the state of Rhode Island:
The Rhode Island Department of Health (HEALTH) has lifted the precautionary boil water advisory (issued on September 4) for Middletown water customers. Portsmouth customers along West Main Road who are supplied by the Newport Water System remain on a precautionary boil water advisory. HEALTH recommends that water being used for drinking, making ice, brushing teeth, cooking, or bathing of infants should be boiled for one minute and allowed to cool before using. Boiling kills bacteria and other organisms in the water. Bottled water can also be used.
Due to a water main break, the water pressure dropped below acceptable limits and therefore, the likelihood for bacterial contamination increases. The water system is working closely with HEALTH to correct the problem as soon as possible.
This boil water advisory is in effect until further notice from HEALTH. Portsmouth water customers are asked to contact neighbors who may not be aware of this advisory.
For information, contact the Station 1 at 845-5826; Julia Forgue at 845-5601; or Ken Mason at 845-5614. For general information about drinking water, contact HEALTH's Information Line at 1-800-942-7434, Monday - Friday, 8:30 a.m. - 4:30 p.m. For information on guidelines for food establishments during and after a boil water advisory, visit http://www.health.ri.gov/environment/dwq/boiladvisory.php

Length: 186 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: PROVIDENCE, RI
Body


The following information was released by the state of Rhode Island:
The Rhode Island Department of Health (HEALTH) is notifying customers of Newport Water System that the precautionary boil water advisory put in place on September 4 has been lifted. The water is safe to use for drinking, cooking and bathing infants and no longer needs to be boiled before use.
Water testing from multiple points in the distribution system confirms that the water system does not contain bacteria. All of the water systems will resume routine testing of the water quality and will continue to report results to HEALTH.
Customers and businesses are advised to: --Flush faucets that have not been used since Saturday, September 4. --Replace water treatment filter cartridges. --Sanitize refrigerator water and ice makers.
