Canal Mutual is one of three water systems placed on boil-water advisories last month after E. coli was found in their wells and in at least one private well in the area. East Bank of Orleans Parish Under Precautionary Boil Water Advisory Until Sunday Afternoon
Targeted News Service
November 20, 2010 Saturday 2:29 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 555 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: NEW ORLEANS
Body


The city of New Orleans issued the following news release:
Mayor Landrieu, Public Health officials, and Sewerage & Water Board officials addressed the media today to update citizens on the precautionary Boil Water Advisory issued for the East Bank of Orleans Parish. The precautionary Boil Water Advisory is expected to be in place until Sunday afternoon at approximately 3:00 pm, when water test results can be verified by the state Department of Health and Hospitals. This does not affect the West Bank.
"I want to stress that this is a precautionary measure and the City is following the protocol required by the state sanitary code," said Mayor Mitch Landrieu. "Based on our conversations with health officials and the Sewerage and Water Board, we are confident that the risk is low."
The State recommends that you disinfect your water by boiling it for one minute and letting it cool down prior to consumption (including drinking, cooking, brushing teeth, bathing or preparing food). Boil water for one full minute in a clean container. The one-minute boil time begins after the water has been brought to a rolling boil. (If there is a flat taste, it can be eliminated by shaking the water in a bottle or pouring it from one container to another.)
"We're uncertain at this point if there was a compromise to the system," said Dr. Takeisha Davis, Regional Medical Director at the Louisiana Office of Public Health. "The major risk is from ingestion, and we think that this risk is very low."
Davis added, "There is little risk to taking a shower, as long as individuals close their mouths and do not ingest the water. However, we recommend that individuals with open wounds or immune system deficiencies take special precautions and avoid showering while the precautionary boil advisory is in effect."
At approximately 7:00 am on Saturday, the Sewerage and Water Board's chemists and technicians began collecting 28 water samples from sites throughout the East Bank. Analysis began at 12:00 PM of all samples. Tests are being conducted at the Board's Water Purification Laboratory. Tests will be incubated for 24 hours to determine if any harmful bacteria are present in the samples. If the tests show that the water is free of harmful bacteria and has a normal chlorine concentration, the precautionary Boil Water Advisory would then be lifted with the approval of the Department of Health and Hospitals (DHH).
At approximately 10:30 pm on Friday, the Sewerage & Water Board lost 25 cycle power at its main water plant, causing low water pressure (as low as 10 pounds per square inch) throughout the East Bank of the City. The Board has restored its 25-cycle power and is also operating on commercial power. According to the Board, water pressure has approached near-normal pressure, as repairs to the electrical system at the main water plant are underway. The Mayor has ordered an after action report to determine what caused the power failure.
The City's Office of Homeland Security and the State Department of Health and Hospitals are in contact with hospital, hotel, restaurant, and tourism officials to help ensure continuity of operations.
For information, citizens can log onto www.nola.gov or   www.swbno.org. Citizens can call 311 (and press zero) or 658-4000.

Much of New Orleans is under a boil-water advisory until at least Sunday afternoon, Mayor Mitch Landrieu said Saturday.

Precautionary Boil Water Advisory Cancelled
Targeted News Service
November 21, 2010 Sunday 2:19 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 286 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: NEW ORLEANS
Body


The city of New Orleans issued the following news release:
Mayor Landrieu, public health officials, and Sewerage &
Water Board officials announced this evening that the precautionary Boil Water Advisory issued for the East Bank of Orleans Parish yesterday has been cancelled. Test results were verified by the state Department of Health and Hospitals.
"After following the protocols of the federal Environmental Protection Agency and the state Department of Health and Hospitals, and after working with doctors, engineers, chemists and other experts, we can report that the water in New Orleans is safe and the precautionary Boil Water Advisory is cancelled," said Mayor Mitch Landrieu.
State health regulations required the precautionary Boil Water Advisory and testing because water pressure dropped below 15 psi (pounds per square inch) which increases the risk of contaminants entering the water system.
At approximately 7:00 am on Saturday, the Sewerage and Water Board's chemists and technicians began collecting 28 water samples from sites throughout the East Bank. In an abundance of caution, a second round of sampling began at 2:00 pm Saturday. Tests were conducted at the Board's Water Purification Laboratory. A 24-hour incubation period is required to determine if any harmful bacteria are present in the samples.
At approximately 10:30 pm on Friday, the Sewerage & Water Board lost 25-cycle power at its main water plant, causing low water pressure (as low as 10 pounds per square inch) throughout the East Bank of the City. According to the Board, water pressure has normalized.
The Mayor has ordered an after action report of the incident.

Mayor Landrieu Releases After-Action Report on Water Incident
Targeted News Service
November 24, 2010 Wednesday 2:17 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 454 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: NEW ORLEANS
Body


The city of New Orleans issued the following news release:
Today, Mayor Landrieu and Sewerage & Water Board officials presented their after-action report following this past weekend's water pressure loss and precautionary boil water advisory on the East Bank of Orleans Parish.
"As this reports shows, all federal and state protocol and procedures were followed," said Mayor Landrieu. "As a consequence, risk to public health was minimized and no illnesses were reported. We are pleased to announce that a new allocation of $3 million from FEMA will provide total rehabilitation of pumps at two critical stations on the East Bank."
Residents and businesses on the East Bank will receive a two-day credit adjustment on their next water bills. S&WB will include a two-day credit adjustment for the average of two-days of usage during the next billing period. The adjustment is for water service only, as sewer service was not interrupted.
At 10:28 pm on Friday, November 19, 2010, operators and engineers manning the Sewerage and Water Board's (S&WB) Carrollton Water Treatment Plant heard loud popping sounds and steam began to fill the boiler room. Interior tubing had broken inside of a boiler, causing the sudden failure of this critical piece of equipment. The loss of this boiler triggered a cascading effect that resulted in the shut down of three of the four pumps moving water to the East Bank of Orleans Parish.
The skilled operators and engineers at S&WB worked well throughout the emergency. They restored four operating pumps at 12:45 am Saturday, within two and half hours of the initial boiler failure. They brought water pressure back to normal levels at 11:17pm on Saturday.
Throughout the incident, water treatment processes at the Carrollton Water Treatment Plant were not affected and finished water entering the distribution system met all water quality regulatory requirements.
The City is again encouraging residents to sign up for NOLAReady text alerts. These text alerts have proven to be valuable supplementary notification for the public, especially when emergencies happen after hours. The public is encouraged to sign up for alerts at www.NolaReady.info or send a blank text to NOLA4U (665248) or call 658-4000.
Other outcomes and next steps in the report include:
* To supplement regular maintenance, operators and engineers have begun the steps necessary to thoroughly inspect all critical equipment including boilers.
* The City and S&WB have put new notification protocol in place with redundancies.

Hamilton Water System Installs Backup
Targeted News Service
November 24, 2010 Wednesday 3:01 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 287 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: HAMILTON, Ohio
Body


The city of Hamilton issued the following news release:
Since the windstorm in September 2008 from the remnants of Hurricane Ike, the City of Hamilton has been installing permanent back-up power generators at our water system pumping stations. We have recently completed the installation of our third such generator and have purchased several portable generators. The South Water Treatment Plant in Fairfield has a large generator capable of not only supplying power to the plant but also can supply power to our electric distribution system during peak electric demands. We have successfully utilized the generators already in place during recent power outages. Without these generators, we would not be able to pump water throughout our system during extended power outages which in turn could cause water outages, boil advisories and greatly limit health & fire protection.
The goal is that by the end of 2011 the entire water system will be able to operate using generators in the event of a power outage. Once the installation of the generators is completed, the city will conduct exercises simulating a citywide power outage and operate the entire water system on the generators.
These installations have been a combined effort by our Water Production and Utility Electrical Systems Divisions. Most of the design, engineering, installation, and purchasing of equipment for these projects was performed in-house by City personnel providing a savings of thousands of dollars for the water customer. We continue to maintain and upgrade various aspects of the water system in an effort to provide high quality water at the lowest practical cost.

Commentary: Crash and learn
New Orleans City Business (New Orleans, LA)
December 2, 2010 Thursday


Copyright 2010 Dolan Media Newswires All Rights Reserved
Section: COMMENTARY
Length: 412 words
Byline: CityBusiness Staff Editorial
Body


Orleans Parish Civil District Court is still sorting out the mess following an Oct. 26 computer system crash. It resulted in a loss of data that researchers need access to to complete real estate transactions.
Meanwhile, title attorneys and Realtors are closing deals conditionally when possible, and some purchases have been delayed indefinitely. While Clerk of Court Dale Atkins says most of the data has been restored, the index for the complete record system must be rebuilt. Without it, there's no way to navigate the existing or restored records.
It's no secret New Orleans lacks the technical infrastructure that is standard in many of its peer cities, but that such a catastrophic collapse took place demands accountability. A critical business sector essentially has been brought to a jarring halt, and it simply isn't good enough to fix what was broken and move forward.
The situation calls for a post-mortem investigation, with a detailed plan of action for how the court will ensure such a meltdown never occurs again. The city just conducted a similar evaluation following a breakdown at the East Bank water treatment facility that led to a boil-water advisory for most residents for nearly two days.
For real estate professionals, the shutdown of mortgage and conveyance records is comparable. Their access to vital information has been down for more than a month, a drought the industry can hardly afford to let linger.
It's easy, almost a habit in New Orleans, to point the finger of blame on years of negligence. But that's no longer an acceptable excuse in a day and age when technological resources are easily accessible. No one expects the Orleans Civil District Court to reinvent the wheel when it comes to official real estate records, but it's not asking too much for our wheel to at least be able to roll. Right now, it's not.
But we caution those in the real estate industry from turning to Baton Rouge for help. Title attorneys and Realtors have called upon Gov. Bobby Jindal to declare a state of emergency in Orleans Parish, triggering a call for outside experts to put the system back together again.
For starters, there's no indication the governor is interested in the real estate records issue in New Orleans or capable of crafting a solution. Also, Atkins is already using resources from the Jefferson Parish Clerk of Court and the Orleans Parish Sheriff's Office to restore records.
It's a good start but far from the permanent fix that's needed.

Load-Date: December 9, 2010


End of Document






BOIL WATER ADVISORY ISSUED FOR PORTIONS OF THE CITY OF HORTON, CITY OF WILLIS
States News Service
December 9, 2010 Thursday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 727 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: TOPEKA, KS
Body


The following information was released by the Kansas Department of Health and Environment:
The Kansas Department of Health and Environment (KDHE) has issued a boil water advisory for the City of Willis and portions of the City of Horton, which are both located in Brown County. The Boil Water Advisory for the City of Horton applies to the Circle Drive area, and areas north of 15th street and west of 1st Avenue East.
The City of Horton is reporting a loss of water pressure which has affected part of the city as well as the City of Willis. Whenever such a loss of pressure occurs, it is possible for contaminants to enter the system. Also during this time, disinfection (chlorine) residuals may drop to levels that are inadequate to protect against bacterial contamination.
When water service is restored, residents in the cities of Horton and Willis served by the affected public water system should observe the following precautions:
Boil water vigorously for one minute prior to use. Boiling longer than three minutes may adversely affect the quality and taste of the water.
Use only boiled water for drinking, brushing teeth, diluting fruit juices, and all other food preparation.
Dispose of ice cubes and do not use ice from a household automatic icemaker. Remake ice cubes with water that has been boiled.
Disinfect dishes and other food contact surfaces by immersion for at least one minute in clean tap water that contains one teaspoon of unscented household bleach per gallon of water.
Water used for bathing does not generally need to be boiled. Supervision of children is necessary while bathing or using backyard pools so water is not ingested. Persons with cuts or severe rashes may wish to consult their physicians.
The advisory will remain in effect until testing of water samples indicates no evidence of contamination and all other conditions which place the systems at risk of contamination are deemed by KDHE officials to be resolved. The City and/or KDHE will notify media when the boil water advisory has been rescinded. Concerned customers may contact the City by telephone at 785-486-2681.
KDHE News Release - Boil Water Advisory Issued for portions of the City of Horton, City of Willis For Immediate Release

DeKalb ordered to clean up sewer; County fined for more than 830 sewage spills.; $700 million upgrades mandated; 11 percent rate increase planned.
The Atlanta Journal-Constitution
December 14, 2010 Tuesday
First Replate Edition


Copyright 2010 The Atlanta Journal-Constitution


Section: NEWS; Pg. 1A
Length: 1410 words
Byline: Megan Matteucci

Staff
Body


The Environmental Protection Agency has fined DeKalb County for more than 830 sewage spills during the past five years and mandated it make repairs to its aging water and sewer system.
On Monday, the U.S. attorney general and the EPA issued a consent decree, ordering DeKalb to improve its sewer system, similar to a federal mandate made against the city of Atlanta several years ago. Failure to meet the decree could mean additional fines of up to $37,500 a day.
The Atlanta Journal-Constitution obtained copies of the consent decree and a settlement agreement, which indicate DeKalb already has agreed to make improvements. The county also agreed to pay a $453,000 fine for the spills and an additional $600,000 to clean up the South River, Snapfinger Creek and the South Fork on Peachtree Creek near Emory University.
The fine will be split between the federal and state governments.
The DeKalb County Commission today is scheduled to vote on $1.35 billion in upgrades to its water and sewer system.
The consent decree calls for about $700 million in upgrades.
County Commissioner Lee May said the vote only says when and how the county will pay, but either way, taxpayers are responsible for the bill.
The upgrades mean an average family's bimonthly bill will go from $165 to $178 this year and then continue to increase 11 percent for the next three years.
On Monday, the EPA filed a 17-page complaint filed against the county, alleging 836 sewage overflows in DeKalb from 2006 to October 2010. The spills, which are in violation of the federal Clean Water Act and the Georgia Water Quality Control Act, emanated from broken manholes and clogged sewer lines, according to the complaint.
The spills pose a "significant threat" to public health because raw sewage has high levels of bacteria that can end up in streets, yards and waterways, the EPA said.
The spills have resulted in thousands of gallons of untreated sewage, including fecal matter and industrial waste spilling into local waterways.
"Unless restrained by an order of the court, DeKalb County will continue to discharge pollutants from point sources without a permit or other authorization," the U.S. attorney's office wrote.
The 104-page consent decree orders the county to make drastic improvements in the next eight years.
The EPA released the documents after the AJC learned that the federal government has been in discussions with the county for about a year.
"The feds are looking closely," May said before the EPA's announcement. "Whenever we have sewage spills, they're watching. If we don't do it, the federal government will come in and make us do it at their prices."
DeKalb CEO Burrell Ellis attributed the spills to the county's 50-year-old sewer system, which he said is one of the oldest and largest in the Southeast. The system includes 2,600 miles of sewer lines, 55,000 manhole covers and 66 lift stations.
"These improvements will ensure long-term protection of public health and the environment," Ellis said Monday. "The consent decree provides a road map to work cooperatively with the EPA and the [Georgia Environmental Protection Division]."
County officials said they plan to work with the federal government and not fight them like Atlanta.
In 1998, former Atlanta Mayor Bill Campbell signed a federal consent decree committing to $4 billion in upgrades to improve water quality. The city has until 2014 to finish the work and is currently seeking a 15-year extension for a small part of the project. Atlanta's federal decree came after a lawsuit filed by the Upper Chattahoochee Riverkeeper. The EPA and state EPD later joined the suit.
DeKalb officials said they have been trying to avoid the high costs and legal battles that plagued Atlanta by moving forward with the work, which includes 80 separate projects. County officials said they hope to take advantage of the current low interest rates and construction costs.
"Sewage overflows are a significant problem in the Southeast because of inadequate and aging infrastructure," Stan Meiburg, deputy regional administrator of the EPA's Southeastern office, said in a statement. "This agreement demonstrates DeKalb County's commitment to address long-standing sewage problems. Ultimately, this will benefit the local community and improve water quality in the Upper Ocmulgee and Chattahoochee watersheds."
In addition to the system's age, the EPA cited problems with fats, oils and greases. County officials said they will use video cameras to find these clogs and begin repairs as soon as the commission votes on the work.
In March, the county called for $1.9 billion in water system upgrades to be paid for by a 110 percent increase in residents' rates over five years, or annual increases of 16 percent. Since then, commissioners have whittled the upgrades down to $1.35 billion with a 11 percent increase in residents' rates.
Half of the work is to make the county's sewers in compliance with federal regulations, said Ted Rhinehart, DeKalb's deputy chief officer of infrastructure. A fourth of the cost will go to upgrade the Snapfinger wastewater treatment plant, which is nearing capacity. The plant has a capacity of 36 million gallons a day and currently averages about 30 million gallons a day.
"We're on borrowed time," Rhinehart told the AJC.
May, chairman of the commission's public works committee, said he recently spoke with former Atlanta Mayor Shirley Franklin, who led the effort to get a sales tax passed to pay for the city's water improvements.
This month, hundreds of DeKalb residents attended community meetings, objecting to the proposed rate increases.
"Whether you call it a rate, a fee, a fine or tax, it's still coming out of the same pocket --- yours and mine," May said.
Commissioner Elaine Boyer, the commission's lone Republican, said she wants to wait on the vote to allow residents to comment and review the decree.
"Only a third of it is mandated by the federal government. In a time of foreclosures, we need to give residents time to review these projects," Boyer said. "But residents are saying they can't afford all of this. I just don't buy this whole $1.4 billion."
Water bill increases may be in addition to a possible tax hike. DeKalb already is facing an estimated $55 million shortfall in next year's budget. Ellis will issue his proposed budget on Wednesday.
In addition to higher costs, further delaying the projects could mean boil water advisories, more leaks and other public health problems, Commissioner Jeff Rader said.
Two weeks ago, the county had to close portions of Second Avenue in Decatur after pipes broke and 40,800 gallons of sewage spilled, according to Water Department records. Last week, the county had to suspend water service for 12 hours to residents near Glenwood Road and Parkhill Drive in Decatur after a water main burst. And a rail section in Decatur is closed this week to repair a water main under the tracks.
May said these spills, along with other spills, have resulted in thousands of dollars in fines from the EPA.
"Their system has very similar problems to those the city of Atlanta has had," said Sally Bethea, executive director of the Upper Chattahoochee Riverkeeper, who sent a letter to the commission endorsing the projects. "What matters is they are moving to fix this critical infrastructure in the county. It's an investment in the future."
Like Atlanta, DeKalb's pipes are aging and don't have the capacity to meet any additional growth beyond the county's 730,000 residents, Rhinehart said. However, DeKalb's sewer system is not in as dire condition as Atlanta's, which had its storm water and sanitary systems combined. In DeKalb, the water systems are separate, which is what the EPA recommends.
Bethea said she is pleased that the Snapfinger upgrades will improve water quality in the South River, which has been closed to swimmers since the summer when tests found fecal matter and industrial waste.
The federal government will collect comments from the public in the next 30 days before finalizing the consent decree. The county must pay the fine, which will come from its operating budget, at the end of the public comment period.
What must be done
The consent decree mandates about $700 million of work, including:
*Identify overflows of untreated sewage and their causes
*Assess and rehabilitate all priority areas within 8 1/2 years
*Improve management, operation and maintenance programs to prevent future overflows
*Respond to overflows when they occur

City of Richland Issues Boil Advisory
Targeted News Service
December 15, 2010 Wednesday 2:14 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 213 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: RICHLAND, Iowa
Body


The Iowa Department of Natural Resources issued the following news release:
The City of Richland in Keokuk County has issued a boil advisory for its drinking water system.
A major water main break early Wednesday caused the water system to lose pressure. Once pressure has been lost within a water system, there is potential for bacterial contamination, prompting the boil advisory.
It is recommended not to drink the water without boiling it first. Bring all water to a boil, let it boil for one minute, and let it cool before using, or use bottled water. Boiled or bottled water should be used for drinking, making ice, brushing teeth, and food preparation until further notice. Boiling kills bacteria and other organisms in the water. The water may be used for bathing and other similar purposes.
General guidelines on ways to lessen the risk of infection by microbes are available from the EPA Safe Drinking Water Hotline at 1(800) 426-4791.
The City of Richland is repairing the water main, and will flush the lines and collect bacteria samples. The boil advisory will remain in place until necessary testing can take place to ensure the water is safe. The city is working with the DNR to resolve the situation.
Copyright Targeted News Services

Water Advisory Ends for Snohomish County Housing Development
Targeted News Service
December 16, 2010 Thursday 9:06 AM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 160 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, Wash.
Body


The Washington state Department of Health issued the following news release:
te release: December 17, 2010 (10-205)
Contacts:
Gordon MacCracken, Communications Office 360-236-4072
Carolyn Cox, Office of Drinking Water 360-236-3162
OLYMPIA - Residents of the Marbello housing development just north of Monroe no longer have to boil their drinking water. A health advisory issued Tuesday has ended because lab tests show the water meets safe drinking water standards.
The advisory was issued after a water main broke, causing an outage. The pressure loss could have allowed contaminated or untreated water to be drawn into the system. The advisory affected only the Marbello housing development, which is off Chain Lakes Road about one mile north of Monroe. About 290 people live there.
Customers who have questions about their water service may call Iliad Inc., which operates the water system, at 206-282-4200.

Precautionary Boil Water Advisory 'Seminole County Southwest Service Area-Apple Valley Water Treatment Plant'
Targeted News Service
December 17, 2010 Friday 11:48 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 221 words
Byline: Targeted News Service
Dateline: SANFORD, Fla.
Body


Seminole County issued the following news release:
A precautionary boil water advisory was issued Friday, December 17, 2010 at 6:00 a.m. due to scheduled water main maintenance in the water distribution system. The distribution system was flushed, and we have commenced taking bacteriological samples as a precautionary measure. (1 service connection was affected).
PWS # 3590039
Subdivision:
Streets: 841 Douglas Ave
District: 3
"Precautionary Boil Water Advisory" door signs were placed on the businesses/residences to inform the customers of this situation and to provide contact information. Larger signs were placed at specific intersections within the service area.
As a precaution, we advise that all water used for drinking, cooking, making ice, brushing teeth, or washing dishes be boiled. A rolling boil of one minute is sufficient. As an alternative bottled water may be used.
This "Precautionary Boil Water Notice" will remain in effect until the problem has been corrected and bacteriological survey shows that the water is safe to drink.
If you have any questions you may contact Seminole County Environmental Services Department at 407.665.2110 between the hours of 8:00 am - 5:00 pm, Monday through Friday, or call 407.665.2767 all other hours.

Pipes, pumps trouble Big Easy; Water, sewage infrastructure slow recovery
USA TODAY
December 17, 2010 Friday
FINAL EDITION


Copyright 2010 Gannett Company, Inc. All Rights Reserved
Section: NEWS; Pg. 3A
Length: 857 words
Byline: Rick Jervis
Body


NEW ORLEANS -- This city's post-Katrina rebuilding has revamped neighborhoods and restored streets and homes from the flood wreckage.
But one area where city leaders say recovery is falling rapidly behind is the city's antiquated sewer and water system. The 100-year-old network of underground pipes, pumps and power plants -- one of the USA's oldest -- was rickety before the 2005 hurricane's floods hit and got worse once they subsided.
The system showed its age last month when a century-old power plant that partly powers the city's water treatment system gave out, throwing the city into a two-day boil-water advisory.
City leaders say New Orleans cannot fully recover from Katrina until a massive, multibillion-dollar upgrade is made to the sewer and water system, first installed at the dawn of the 20th century. Federal rebuilding funds are paying only for a patchwork of repairs, and the city doesn't have the resources to do it alone, says New Orleans Mayor Mitch Landrieu, a Democrat.
As with many other cities, New Orleans' aging infrastructure is low on the priority list in Washington, he says. "When the city is sitting on age-old infrastructure, something's going to give. That's true around the country," Landrieu says. "Congress and the federal government have not made it a priority. We're falling very, very far behind."
More than 1,000 aging water and sewer systems around the country need urgent upgrades, says Ken Kirk, executive director of the National Association of Clean Water Agencies. With the passing of the Clean Water Act in 1972, the federal government once paid about 75% of a municipality's upkeep of water and sewer treatment systems, Kirk says. Today, that number is closer to 3%, he says.
The USA's drinking water supply is threatened daily, Kirk says. Cities such as Atlanta, Baltimore, Boston, Kansas City, New York and Philadelphia have antiquated systems that are in dire need of renovation. Across the country, there is a $500 billion to $1 trillion need to upgrade systems, Kirk says. Local governments should also be spending more, he says.
With the federal government in deficit-reduction mode and local municipalities battling their own budget shortfalls, that investment seems unlikely anytime soon, Kirk says.
"We are in a critical situation," he says. "If those systems break down, you go back to a time when people didn't have running water or toilets and where breakouts of major diseases like cholera were common. I don't think anyone wants to go back to that time."
Sen. James Inhofe, R-Okla., says Congress has vastly underfinanced infrastructure. Inhofe, the ranking Republican on the Senate's Environment & Public Works Committee, says he is working on two bills that will direct more funds to such projects, but Washington's current cost-cutting climate makes it a tough sell.
The New Orleans system was installed in the early 1900s, says Joseph Becker, general superintendent of the Sewerage and Water Board. The network includes a drainage system with 23 pumps that can move 400,000 gallons a second -- enough to fill the Superdome in under an hour -- a necessity for a city mostly below sea level, Becker says. During Hurricane Katrina, the pumps took just six days to clear out the floodwaters that covered 80% of the city, he says.
The network also collects water from the Mississippi River, cleans it and delivers it to homes across the city using a power plant built more than a century ago, Becker says. That power plant gave out the evening of Nov. 19, dropping water pressure across the city and propelling city leaders to call a boil-water advisory.
The Federal Emergency Management Agency has approved about $300 million to repair more than 1,600 miles of water mains damaged by Katrina, he says. Much more money is needed for a permanent fix, including $180 million to replace the power plant that failed last month, he says. "We feel the correct way to handle the repairs is not by simply putting Band-Aids over small sections of the system," Becker says. "The United States doesn't address their infrastructure issues. It's sort of out of sight, out of mind."
The federal government is investing heavily to revamp the city's underground drainage canals, says Stan Green, a project manager for the Army Corps of Engineers in New Orleans. The $1 billion project was approved in the late 1990s. It will add to the current system of canals and culverts that help drain the city during heavy storms, he says. "We've made significant improvements," he says.
New Orleans' entire water and sewer system needs an overhaul, says Bhaskar Kura, a civil engineering professor and director of the Maritime Environmental Resources and Information Center at the University of New Orleans.
The American Society of Civil Engineers recently graded the nation's drinking water and wastewater systems each a "D-" on its national infrastructure report card, he says.
"Twenty years back, developing nations would look at the United States like, wow, they have all this innovative infrastructure," Kura says. "But, as time passed, some of these infrastructures have become old, and we haven't invested enough."

PHOTO, B/W, Cheryl Gerber for USA TODAY

WATER ADVISORY ENDS FOR SNOHOMISH COUNTY HOUSING DEVELOPMENT
States News Service
December 17, 2010 Friday


Copyright 2010 States News Service
Length: 125 words
Byline: States News Service
Dateline: OLYMPIA, WA
Body


The following information was released by the Washington State Department of Health:
Residents of the Marbello housing development just north of Monroe no longer have to boil their drinking water. A health advisory issued Tuesday has ended because lab tests show the water meets safe drinking water standards.
The advisory was issued after a water main broke, causing an outage. The pressure loss could have allowed contaminated or untreated water to be drawn into the system. The advisory affected only the Marbello housing development, which is off Chain Lakes Road about one mile north of Monroe. About 290 people live there.
Customers who have questions about their water service may call Iliad Inc., which operates the water system, at 206-282-4200.

CITY OF RICHLAND LIFTS BOIL ADVISORY
US State News
December 20, 2010 Monday 7:32 PM EST


Copyright 2010 Targeted News Service LLC All Rights Reserved
Length: 119 words
Body


RICHLAND, Iowa, Dec. 20 -- The Iowa Department of Natural Resources issued the following news release:
The City of Richland in Keokuk County has lifted the boil advisory for its drinking water system.
Testing of the repaired system after it had been flushed indicates no bacteria in the water, meaning residents can once again use tap water for drinking and cooking.
A boil advisory was issued Wednesday, December 15, when a major water main break caused the water system to lose pressure. Once pressure has been lost in a water system, there is potential for bacterial contamination. PWS # 3590571-01
Subdivision: Tuskawilla Point

New Water Line Accesses Knott County Water Source To Help Alleviate Some Of Countys Water Woes
Letcher County Community News-Press (Cromona, Kentucky)
December 22, 2010


Copyright 2010 SmallTownPapers, Inc.
All Rights Reserved
SmallTownPapers, Inc.
Copyright 2010 Letcher County Community News-Press


This content, including derivations, may not be stored or distributed in any manner, disseminated, published, broadcast, rewritten or reproduced without express, written consent from STPNS
Length: 709 words
Byline: Letcher County Community News-Press staff
Body


Recent water issues for residents in the Blackey community are still of some concern to people wanting to know just how the trouble began. For areas with aging water systems or in which one community relies on another to receive water services, the scramble to restore water to the area was trying, especially when efforts to get customers back on line took place during harsh weather conditions.
Phillip Back, Chairman of the Letcher County Water and Sewer Commission said that trouble for the Blackey area was due to more than one issue. Back explained that the loss of service came to a head when a water line break in the Whitesburg area on Thursday, December 9, caused the 250-300 customers in the Blackey area to feel the effects.
For the people of Blackey, the challenge to get water into the area started well before December. "The Blackey Plant Operator broke a bone three months ago, and has been off," explained Back. "We've been buying all our water from Whitesburg. We haven't had anyone to operate the plant because they must be certified." The absence of a plant operator to help service customers started the events which led to Blackey's water loss.
Another reason in the disruption of service was actually due to the county's efforts to upgrade its infrastructurewhile at the time was considered an inconveniencelater turned out to play in the favor of getting residents back on line. Back said that Stotts Construction Company, hired to "interconnect the Knott and Letcher County system" came in on Saturday, December 11 for a road bore and completed the job Saturday night. The rail road bore helped to bring water to the Letcher County system from neighboring Knott county, and services a large area of the county including the Low Gap and Collie areas towards Isom, Jeremiah and Blackey.
To further complicate matters, a break then oc-cured in the Low Gap area, which had to be repaired. After the interconnection was made, Back said that residents had "a boil water advisory," which was lifted Sunday afternoon," December 12.
"It takes some time for lines to be completed, emptied out... you have to bleed the lines, the fire hydrants. It took time to get them done." Back explained that lines and hydrants are required to be bled whenever there is a disruption of service in order to clear the lines for consumers to use. Back added that "all the water employees, and some or all of the county's recycling employees, were involved in trying to restore service to Blackey customers as quickly as possible. Also on hand to help aid in water restoration were Letcher County Judge Executive Jim Ward and Deputy Judge Eddie Meade, who helped to bleed hydrants to get customers back on line. All this has put more than just a strain on customers who were without service. Back added that since the trouble began the cost of serving the 250-300 Blackey area water customers has "nearly doubled." According to Back, the Blackey plant has been operating in the hole for the past year and is in need of "major upgrades."
However, Back mentioned an upside to the challenges recently faced by Blackey residents which is that the water situation is "under control now" thanks to the interconnection from Knott County."
The Hwy 1410 interconnection, along Trace Fork Road, adds a 600,000 gallon water tank to the county's water supply, which Back said should supply all the lower end of Letcher County.
With the new plant located at Carr Fork Lake which has been in operation for nearly a year, Back feels that Letcher County residents should be "in pretty good shape."
Back says that they have been doing everything within their power to ensure Blackey residents have the service which they require. "The state, Division of Water, and county officials support our efforts and feel we're going the in the right direction," he said. Despite all the setbacks, a number of people have played a role in trying to provide all of Letcher County with an infrastructure that is up-to-date, giving citizens the clean drinking water they deserve.
A meeting for the water board is scheduled for Wednesday, December 22, at 6 p.m., at the Letcher County Courthouse, District Court for those interested in learning more about the issues affecting the county's water system.

2nd drop in 5 weeks at N.O. water plant
The Associated Press State & Local Wire
December 23, 2010 Thursday 4:49 PM GMT


Copyright 2010 Associated Press All Rights Reserved
Section: STATE AND REGIONAL
Length: 425 words
Dateline: NEW ORLEANS
Body


Many New Orleans homes and businesses across New Orleans lost water pressure briefly Wednesday night after the failure one of the four huge turbines that powers the Sewerage & Water Board's pumps.
Unlike a Nov. 19 failure that brought a 41-hour advisory to boil water, this one was fixed in 30 minutes, said Joe Becker, general superintendent for the board. He said a key backup pump was switched on in minutes; in November, that pump was being repaired.
Both problems affected the east bank, where most of the city is located. The west bank Algiers neighborhood has a separate treatment plant and was not affected.
Although the backup pump kept water pressure safe, the board's in-house power plant shut down for about two hours.
It was only the fourth failure since the facility opened at the turn of the 20th century. All four shutdowns were after Hurricane Katrina.
The water purification plant runs on power purchased from Entergy New Orleans. But 25-Hertz power, which was common in the late 1800s, drives the motors that keep huge pumps sucking water from the Mississippi River and smaller pumps pushing purified water into pipes serving homes and businesses.
In-house power also supports about half the city's drainage capacity via 115 miles of underground conduit, including lines that run under the river. The buried wires run from the power plant at South Claiborne Avenue near the Jefferson Parish line to many of the city's 23 drainage pump stations.
The power plant generates electricity by running tap water through enormous boilers, which create steam to run four turbines that produce 25-cycle power. Natural gas purchased from Entergy is used to start boilers and turbines, which run singly or in tandem depending on how much power the system needs.
Once the equipment is up and running, it relies on self-generated steam and a series of natural gas feeds to stay online.
Becker said one turbine was running Wednesday night. When it broke, it immediately shut down two outflow pumps. The backup pump can run either on in-house power or electricity from Entergy. It had been repaired by last week, becker said.
Becker said the broken turbine apparently failed because of an internal electrical malfunction. He said its copper wire coils probably will have to be rewound, a two- to three-month process that must be handled off-site by a contractor, he said.
Such work amounts to routine maintenance, "but we just haven't been able to afford to take this turbine for rewinding," Becker said.
Information from: The Times-Picayune, http://www.nola.com

New Orleans water pressure restored
The Associated Press State & Local Wire
December 23, 2010 Thursday 10:49 AM GMT


Copyright 2010 Associated Press All Rights Reserved
Section: STATE AND REGIONAL
Length: 113 words
Dateline: NEW ORLEANS
Body


Water pressure in New Orleans is back to normal after dropping for the second time in just over a month in many parts of the city.
The city's Sewerage and Water Board said a problem at one of their stations resulted in some residents experiencing no water or extremely low water pressure Wednesday night. The problem affected the entire New Orleans area except the Algiers neighborhood, which is on the west bank of the Mississippi River. But pressure was restored soon after it dropped and this time there was no boil water advisory issued.
In late November a longer-lasting drop in pressure resulted in a precautionary boil water advisory while water was tested for contamination.

New Orleans residents report low water pressure
The Associated Press State & Local Wire
December 23, 2010 Thursday 3:43 AM GMT


Copyright 2010 Associated Press All Rights Reserved
Section: STATE AND REGIONAL
Length: 144 words
Dateline: NEW ORLEANS
Body


The city's Sewerage and Water Board says a problem at one of their stations has resulted in some residents experiencing no water or extremely low water pressure.
The city says the problem is affecting the entire New Orleans area except the Algiers neighborhood, which is on the west bank of the Mississippi River.
Sewerage officials say water pressure at the station is "coming back up," but there's no word on when it will be operating normally.
This is the second time in two months that New Orleans has experienced such problems. In November, the city ordered a boil-water advisory when the water pressure plummeted across the city's east bank.
Mayor Mitch Landrieu has said he will lobby Congress for funding to repair the antiquated infrastructure for the sewerage and water board. Most of the equipment that failed in November was installed between 1920 and 1960.

Pinellas hopes to narrow boil water area today
The Tampa Tribune (Florida)
December 26, 2010 Sunday
FINAL EDITION


Copyright 2010 Times Publishing Company
Section: METRO; Pg. 5
Length: 776 words
Byline: HOWARD ALTMAN AND JOSH GREEN, The News Center
Body


About 100,000 homes are affected by a broken main
BY HOWARD ALTMAN
The Tampa Tribune
AND JOSH GREEN
News Channel 8
Pinellas County Utilities officials hope today to be able to reduce the area affected after a 48-inch water main broke in Largo on Thursday.
Some 100,000 homes had little or no water pressure through Christmas Day, creating a situation where microbes could accumulate, causing health hazards such as stomach cramps, nausea and diarrhea,officials said. They issued the boil water notice as a result.
Kevin Becotte, Pinellasutilities director, said Saturday, "We're required by law to do two days of sampling. We did one set of sampling yesterday and we got the results back today. Those were favorable. We're looking at getting the second set back tomorrow (Sunday) and we'll have the results at that time."
Results should be known this morning. Depending on what they are, officials said they may be able to reduce thearea of the boil water advisory, a news release states.
Officials can use those results to focus on problem areas and perhaps allow portions of southern Pinellas to discontinue boiling water because test samples are collected throughout thewater system.
About 38 properties -- mostly commercial, industrial and an RV park -- serviced by Pinellas County Utilitiesare without water, but it is important for people with little or no water pressure to boil water, pending test results, officials say.
Once the water main is fixed, the county will fix Belcher Road, which has been closed to traffic between East Bay Drive and Ulmerton Road.
Becotte said it will be later in the week, possibly Friday, before the road opens again. He cautioned people heading to work on Monday to avoid that area of Belcher.
The water main break is affecting water customers who do not receivewater from Pinellas and don't need to boil water.
While communities north of Belleair were not affected, some St. Petersburg residents have received reverse 911 calls warning them to boilwater, said Dave Baker, a Pinellas communications spokesman.
He said the 911 system does not always distinguish between residents of the city of St. Petersburg and those of unincorporated St. Petersburg, who use Pinellas County Utilities water.
Anyone paying water bills to the city of St. Petersburg can ignore the warning, Baker said.
The same applies to Gulfport, which buys water from St. Petersburg, Gulfport's website states.
Until the repair is made, officials urge customers to conserve water. A water distribution point is the county utilities' general maintenancesite, 6730 142nd Ave. N. The site is open from noon to 8 p.m. today.
haltman@tampatrib.com
(813) 259-7629
jgreen@wfla.com
(813) 221-5788
(CHART) POTABLE WATER TIPS
If you're under the boil water order, here are answers to questions on how to and whether you need to boil water:
For how long should I boil water and what if I don't have power?
Bring water to a full rolling boil for at least one minute to kill most infectious organisms (germs). For areas without power, disinfect the tap water by adding eight drops, about one eighth of a teaspoon, of plain unscented household bleach per gallon of water and allow the water to stand for 30 minutes. If the water is cloudy, repeat the procedure. Use a container that has a cap or cover for disinfecting and storing water to be used for drinking. This will prevent contamination. If your well was flooded, boiling the water is the safest action, since disinfection does not kill certain parasites.
Can I wash my hands with tap water?
To clean your hands, vigorous hand washing with soap is fine; if you're washing your hands to prepare food, use water that has been boiled and cooled or use bottled or disinfected water with soap.
What about washing dishes or clothes?
Rinse hand-washed dishes for a minute in a bleach solution (1 tablespoon bleach per gallon of water) and let dishes completely air dry. Most household dishwashers do not reach the proper temperature to sanitize dishes, though the drying cycle of the dishwasher helps disinfect and clean dishes. It is safe to wash clothes in tap water.
Is it safe to bathe and shave using tap water?
Yes, as long as you do not swallow the water or get it in your eyes, nose or mouth. People with surgical wounds, who are immunosuppressed or who have chronic illnesses may want to use bottled or boiled water.
Can I wash off fruits and vegetables with tap water? What about making ice?
No. Use boiled water that has cooled, or water that is bottled or has been sanitized with the bleach solution.
Pinellas County Utilities

Pinellas crews working to replace water main
The Tampa Tribune (Florida)
December 29, 2010 Wednesday
FINAL EDITION


Copyright 2010 Times Publishing Company
Section: METRO; Pg. 8
Length: 200 words
Byline: staff reports
Body


Job may not be finished until the end of the week
From staff reports
CLEARWATER -- Crews worked most of Monday night toward replacing a 48-inch water main that burst Thursday, but the job isn't expected to be finished until the end of the week.
Belcher Road, between East Bay Drive and Ulmerton Road, is not expected to reopen until next week. The rupture opened up a 15-foot-deep hole, spanning five to six lanes.
The main ruptured at Belcher and 142nd Avenue North in Largo, prompting a days-long, boil water advisory that affected all Pinellas County Utilities customers in the southern part of the county.
The advisory since has been lifted.
Residents who buy their water from the city of St. Petersburg were not affected.
Overnight Monday, crews worked to remove the concrete surrounding the damaged main. A 26-foot-long section of replacement pipe is expected to be installed by the end of the week, said Paul Giuliani, who is overseeing the project.
Ten businesses in the vicinity of the ruptured main are still without water; workers are installing temporary water lines for their benefit.
